Biden is a Democrat who served as Barack Obama’s 47th vice president from 2009 to 2017 and previously represented Delaware in the United States Senate from 1973 to 2009. From 1987 to 1995, he oversaw the Senate Judiciary Committee. During President Barack Obama’s Senate tenure, Biden wielded considerable power in foreign policy. The Vice President was the driving force behind the passing of the Violent Crime Control and Law Enforcement Act. We are here to help you celebrate the President’s special day.\n\n## Fast Facts\n\nFull Name:\n\nJoseph Robinette Biden Jr.\n\nNickname:\n\nUncle-in-Chief, Amtrak Joe, Cup of Joe\n\nBirth date:\n\nNovember 20, 1942\n\nAge:\n\n82\n\nZodiac Sign:\n\nScorpio\n\nHeight:\n\n5\' 11"\n\nRelationship Status:\n\nMarried\n\nNet Worth:\n\n$9 million\n\nJoseph\'s Social Media:\n\n## Background\n\nJoseph Robinette Biden Jr. was born in Scranton, Pennsylvania, to Catherine Eugenia “Jean” and Joseph Robinette Biden Sr. He is the oldest child in a Catholic family, with a sister, Valerie, and two brothers, Francis and James. Jean was of Irish ancestry, while Joseph Sr. was of English, French, and Irish ancestry. Biden’s father had been wealthy, but suffered financial setbacks around the time Biden was born, and the family spent several years living with Biden’s maternal grandparents. During the 1950s, Scranton experienced economic decline, and Biden’s father was unable to find steady work. Beginning in 1953, when Biden was ten years old, the family resided in an apartment in Claymont, Delaware, before relocating to a home in nearby Mayfield. Biden Sr. later became a successful used-car salesman, keeping the family in the middle class.\n\nBiden was a standout halfback and wide receiver for Archmere Academy in Claymont. Despite being a poor student, he served as class president in his junior and senior years. He received his diploma in 1961. He briefly played freshman football at the University of Delaware. He graduated with a Bachelor of Arts degree in 1965 with a double major in history and political science and a minor in English. Biden has a stutter, which he has been working on since his early twenties. He claims he reduced it by reciting poetry in front of a mirror, but some observers believe it had an impact on his performance in the Democratic Party presidential debates in 2020.\n\nBiden became the 46th president of the United States on January 20, 2021. He is the oldest person to hold the position, at the age of 78. He is the first man since George H. W. Bush to serve as both vice president and president, and the second non-incumbent vice president to be elected president after Richard Nixon in 1968. Due to COVID-19 precautions as well as massively increased security measures due to a threat of widespread civil unrest, Biden’s inauguration was “a muted affair, unlike any previous inauguration.” Biden took the Oath of Office on the west steps of the Capitol and delivered an inaugural address, but there were no spectators on the Mall and no parades or inaugural balls. Donald Trump did not attend the inauguration, making him the first outgoing president since 1869 to do so.\n\n## Career timeline\n\n1965\n\nHe Earns His Bachelor’s Degree\n\nBiden graduates from the University of Delaware in Newark with a Bachelor of Arts degree in history and political science, and a minor in English.\n\n1968\n\nHe Gets a Juris Doctor\n\nBiden graduates from Syracuse University College of Law, where he ranks 76th in his class of 85, and is admitted to the Delaware bar in 1969.\n\n1972\n\nHe Becomes a Junior U.S. Senator\n\nBiden defeats Republican incumbent J. Caleb Boggs to become Delaware\'s junior senator, the only Democrat willing to take on Boggs.\n\n1988\n\nHe Declares His Democratic Presidential Candidacy\n\nBiden formally declares his candidacy for the Democratic presidential nomination; his moderate image, speaking ability, and high profile as chair of the Senate Judiciary Committee make him a strong candidate.\n\n2008\n\nNomination for Vice President\n\nObama announces Biden as his running mate, and he is officially nominated for vice president by voice vote on August 27 at the Democratic National Convention in Denver.\n\n2021\n\nBecoming the United States President\n\nBiden is sworn in as the United States 46th president on January 20, the oldest person to hold the position, at the age of 78.\n\n## Why We Love Joe Biden\n\n1. ### He was awarded the highest civilian honor\n\n\n\nFormer President Barack Obama presented Biden with the Presidential Medal of Freedom, the nation\'s highest civilian honor. This was just days before the end of Obama’s second term.\n\n2. ### He fights violence against women\n\n\n\nIn 1994, Biden co-sponsored the Violence Against Women Act with Republican Senator Orrin Hatch of Utah. The law, which was included in a larger crime bill, provided $1.6 billion to investigate and prosecute violent crimes against women, imposed automatic and mandatory restitution on those convicted, and allowed victims to sue their attackers in civil court even if prosecutors did not pursue criminal charges.\n\n3. ### He led the National Cancer Moonshot Initiative\n\n\n\nDuring his tenure as vice president, Biden was given the authority to lead the National Cancer Moonshot Initiative in 2016. He was to act as a catalyst for cancer research by expediting discoveries, promoting greater collaboration, and making research more transparent between researchers and the public.\n\n\n## 5 Surprising Facts\n\n1. ### He is the country\'s second Catholic president\n\n\n\nBiden is the second Catholic president in American history, the first being John F. Kennedy.\n\n2. ### He had brain surgery\n\n\n\nBiden was taken to Walter Reed Army Medical Center in February 1988 after experiencing several episodes of increasingly severe neck pain, and he underwent surgery to repair a leaking intracranial berry aneurysm.\n\n3. ### He has a weakness for ice cream\n\n\n\nInstead of smoking or consuming alcohol, Biden has a weakness for chocolate chip ice cream, so much so that his campaign spent $10,000 on ice cream, primarily for donors, “Eater” reported.\n\n4. ### He is a published author\n\n\n\nHe has written nine books on his life experiences, including "Promise Me, Dad," in which Biden describes his son’s struggle with cancer, as well as how he coped after his son passed away.\n\n5. ### His dog made history\n\n\n\nMajor, one of Biden\'s two German Shepherds, is a rescue dog and is the first rescue dog to enter the White House.\n\n\n## Joe Biden FAQs\n\n### Was Joe Biden married before Jill Biden?\n\nBiden was married twice, first to Neilia Hunter in 1966 until her passing in a car accident, and later to Jill Biden in 1977.\n\n### Was Joe Biden Trump\'s vice president?\n\nBiden served as vice president twice, but never for Donald Trump; he served as vice president during both terms of Obama’s presidency.\n\n### What is Joe Biden’s slogan?\n\nDuring the presidential elections, Biden’s campaign slogan was “Our Best Days Still Lie Ahead,” “Battle for the Soul of the Nation,” and “No Malarkey!” “Build Back Better,” and “Unite for a Better America.”\n\n## Joe Biden’s birthday dates\n\n| Year | Date | Day |\n| --- | --- | --- |\n| 2025 | November 20 | Thursday |\n| 2026 | November 20 | Friday |\n| 2027 | November 20 | Saturday |\n| 2028 | November 20 | Monday |\n| 2029 | November 20 | Tuesday |\n\n## Other [US President](https://nationaltoday.com/us-president/) Birthdays\n\nRonald Reagan Birthday\n\nThis ex-Hollywood actor turned POTUS can rest in peace knowing he achieved the highest feat.\n\n[See More](https://nationaltoday.com/birthday/ronald-reagan/)\n\nThomas Jefferson Birthday\n\nHe is remembered for being honest and good-hearted and for his social and political achievements\n\n[See More](https://nationaltoday.com/birthday/thomas-jefferson/)\n\nDonald Trump Birthday\n\nEveryone has an opinion about the 45th President of the United States, Donald Trump!\n\n[See More](https://nationaltoday.com/birthday/donald-trump/)\n\nGeorge W. [Supreme Court candidates](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Joe_Biden_Supreme_Court_candidates) - [Executive Office](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_Executive_Office_appointments_by_Joe_Biden) - [U.S. attorneys](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_United_States_attorneys_appointed_by_Joe_Biden) [Presidential campaigns](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Joe_Biden_presidential_campaigns) - [1988](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Joe_Biden_1988_presidential_campaign) - [primaries](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1988_Democratic_Party_presidential_primaries) - [2008](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Joe_Biden_2008_presidential_campaign) - [primaries](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2008_Democratic_Party_presidential_primaries) - [2020](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Joe_Biden_2020_presidential_campaign) - [primaries](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2020_Democratic_Party_presidential_primaries) - [election](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2020_United_States_presidential_election) - [sexual misconduct allegation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Joe_Biden_sexual_misconduct_allegation) - [Ukraine conspiracy theory](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Biden%E2%80%93Ukraine_conspiracy_theory) - [convention](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2020_Democratic_National_Convention) - [debates](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2020_United_States_presidential_debates) - [endorsements](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_Joe_Biden_2020_presidential_campaign_endorsements) - [VP selection](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2020_Democratic_Party_vice_presidential_candidate_selection) - [2024](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Joe_Biden_2024_presidential_campaign) - [primaries](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2024_Democratic_Party_presidential_primaries) - [debate](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2024_United_States_presidential_debates#June_27:_First_presidential_debate_(CNN,_Atlanta)) - [endorsements](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_Joe_Biden_2024_presidential_campaign_primary_endorsements) - [opposition](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_Democrats_who_opposed_the_Joe_Biden_2024_presidential_campaign) - [withdrawal](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Withdrawal_of_Joe_Biden_from_the_2024_United_States_presidential_election) |\n\n**Joseph Robinette Biden Jr.**[\\[a\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-1) (born November 20, 1942) is an American politician who served as the 46th [president of the United States](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/President_of_the_United_States) from 2021 to 2025. A member of the [Democratic Party](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Democratic_Party_(United_States)), he represented [Delaware](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Delaware) in the [United States Senate](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_Senate) from 1973 to 2009 and also served as the 47th [vice president](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vice_President_of_the_United_States) under President [Barack Obama](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama) from 2009 to 2017.\n\nBorn in [Scranton, Pennsylvania](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Scranton,_Pennsylvania), Biden graduated from the [University of Delaware](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/University_of_Delaware) in 1965 and the [Syracuse University College of Law](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Syracuse_University_College_of_Law) in 1968. He was elected to the [New Castle County Council](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/New_Castle_County_Council) in 1970 and the [U.S. Senate in 1972](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1972_United_States_Senate_election_in_Delaware). [As a senator](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/US_Senate_career_of_Joe_Biden), Biden chaired the Senate [Judiciary Committee](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_Senate_Committee_on_the_Judiciary) and [Foreign Relations Committee](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_Senate_Committee_on_Foreign_Relations). He drafted and led passage of the [Violent Crime Control and Law Enforcement Act](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Violent_Crime_Control_and_Law_Enforcement_Act) and the [Violence Against Women Act](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Violence_Against_Women_Act). Biden also oversaw six [U.S. Supreme Court](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/U.S._Supreme_Court) confirmation hearings, including contentious [hearings for Robert Bork](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Robert_Bork_Supreme_Court_nomination) and [Clarence Thomas](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Clarence_Thomas_Supreme_Court_nomination). He opposed the [Gulf War](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gulf_War) in 1991 but voted in favor of the [Iraq War Resolution](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iraq_War_Resolution) in 2002. Biden ran unsuccessfully for the [1988](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1988_Democratic_Party_presidential_primaries) and [2008 Democratic presidential nominations](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2008_Democratic_Party_presidential_primaries). In 2008, Obama chose him as his running mate, and Biden was a close counselor to Obama [as vice president](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vice_presidency_of_Joe_Biden). In the [2020 presidential election](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2020_United_States_presidential_election), Biden chose [Kamala Harris](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kamala_Harris) as his running mate, and they defeated [Republican](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Republican_Party_(United_States)) incumbents [Donald Trump](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump) and [Mike Pence](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mike_Pence).\n\nAs president, Biden signed the [American Rescue Plan Act](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/American_Rescue_Plan_Act_of_2021) in response to the [COVID-19 pandemic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/COVID-19_pandemic_in_the_United_States) and [subsequent recession](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/COVID-19_recession). He signed bipartisan bills on [infrastructure](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Infrastructure_Investment_and_Jobs_Act) and [manufacturing](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/CHIPS_and_Science_Act). Biden proposed the [Build Back Better Act](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Build_Back_Better_Act), aspects of which were incorporated into the [Inflation Reduction Act](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Inflation_Reduction_Act) that he signed into law in 2022. He [appointed Ketanji Brown Jackson](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ketanji_Brown_Jackson_Supreme_Court_nomination) to the [Supreme Court of the United States](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Supreme_Court_of_the_United_States). In [his foreign policy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Foreign_policy_of_the_Joe_Biden_administration), the U.S. reentered the [Paris Agreement](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Paris_Agreement) and enacted the [New Atlantic Charter](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/New_Atlantic_Charter). Biden oversaw the [complete withdrawal of U.S. troops](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2020%E2%80%932021_U.S._troop_withdrawal_from_Afghanistan) that ended the [war in Afghanistan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/War_in_Afghanistan_(2001%E2%80%932021)), leading to [the Taliban seizing control](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2021_Taliban_offensive). He [responded to the Russian invasion of Ukraine](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_and_the_Russian_invasion_of_Ukraine) by imposing [sanctions on Russia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/International_sanctions_during_the_Russian_invasion_of_Ukraine) and authorizing [aid to Ukraine](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_military_aid_to_Ukraine_during_the_Russo-Ukrainian_War). During the [Gaza war](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gaza_war), Biden condemned the actions of [Hamas](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hamas) as terrorism, [strongly supported Israel](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_support_for_Israel_in_the_Gaza_war), and sent limited humanitarian aid to the [Gaza Strip](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gaza_Strip). A temporary [ceasefire proposal](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/January_2025_Gaza_war_ceasefire) he backed was adopted shortly before his presidency ended.\n\n[Concerns about Biden\'s age and health](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Age_and_health_concerns_about_Joe_Biden) persisted throughout his presidency. He became the first president to turn 80 years old while in office. He began his presidency with majority support, but saw his approval ratings decline significantly throughout his presidency, partially due to public frustration over [inflation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2021-2023_inflation_surge), which peaked at 9.1% in June 2022 before dropping to 2.9% by the end of his presidency. Biden initially [ran for reelection](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Joe_Biden_2024_presidential_campaign) and, after the [Democratic primaries](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2024_Democratic_Party_presidential_primaries), became the party\'s presumptive nominee in the [2024 presidential election](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2024_United_States_presidential_election). After his performance in the [first presidential debate](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2024_Joe_Biden%E2%80%93Donald_Trump_presidential_debate), renewed scrutiny from across the political spectrum about his age and health led him to [withdraw his candidacy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Withdrawal_of_Joe_Biden_from_the_2024_United_States_presidential_election). In 2022 and 2024, Biden\'s administration was [ranked favorably](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Historical_rankings_of_presidents_of_the_United_States#Scholar_survey_summary) by historians and scholars, diverging from [unfavorable public assessments](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_presidential_approval_rating) of his tenure. He is the [oldest living former U.S. president](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_presidents_of_the_United_States_by_age#Age_of_presidents), the [oldest living former U.S. vice president](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_vice_presidents_of_the_United_States_by_age), and the oldest person to have served as president.\n\n## Early life (1942–1965)\n\nMain article: [Early life and career of Joe Biden](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Early_life_and_career_of_Joe_Biden)\n\nJoseph Robinette Biden Jr. was born on November 20, 1942,[\\[1\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-cong-bio-2) at St. Mary\'s Hospital in [Scranton, Pennsylvania](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Scranton,_Pennsylvania),[\\[2\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWitcover20105-3) to Catherine Eugenia "Jean" Biden ([née](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Birth_name#Maiden_and_married_names)\xa0Finnegan)[\\[3\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-4) and Joseph Robinette Biden Sr.[\\[4\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-5) He is the oldest child in a [Catholic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Catholic_Church) family of mostly Irish descent. Biden has a sister, [Valerie](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Valerie_Biden_Owens), and two brothers, [James](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/James_Biden) and Francis.[\\[5\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWitcover20108%E2%80%939-6)\n\n### Home life\n\nJoseph Sr. had been wealthy, and the family purchased a home in the affluent Long Island suburb of [Garden City, New York](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Garden_City,_New_York), in 1946.[\\[6\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-7) After he suffered business setbacks around the time Biden was seven years old,[\\[7\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-8)[\\[8\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-promises2008-9)[\\[9\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWitcover20107%E2%80%938-10) the family lived with Jean\'s parents in Scranton for several years.[\\[10\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-nyt-father-11) Scranton fell into economic decline during the 1950s, and Joseph Sr. could not find steady work.[\\[11\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-ap-scranton-12) Beginning in 1953, when Biden was ten,[\\[12\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-13) the family lived in an apartment in [Claymont, Delaware](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Claymont,_Delaware), before moving to a house in nearby [Mayfield, Delaware](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mayfield,_Delaware).[\\[b\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-16) Joseph Sr. later became a successful [used-car salesman](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Used-car_salesman), maintaining the family in a middle-class lifestyle.[\\[10\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-nyt-father-11)[\\[11\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-ap-scranton-12)[\\[15\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-aap08-bio-17)\n\n### Sports and young adulthood\n\nAt [Archmere Academy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Archmere_Academy) in Claymont,[\\[16\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWitcover201027,_32-18) Biden played baseball and was a standout [halfback](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Halfback_(American_football)) and [wide receiver](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wide_receiver) on the [high school football](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/High_school_football) team.[\\[10\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-nyt-father-11)[\\[17\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-19) Though a poor student, he was [class president](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Class_president) in his junior and senior years.[\\[18\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWitcover201040%E2%80%9341-20)[\\[19\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-FOOTNOTETaylor199099-21) He graduated in 1961.[\\[18\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWitcover201040%E2%80%9341-20) At the [University of Delaware](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/University_of_Delaware) in [Newark](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Newark,_Delaware), Biden briefly played freshman football[\\[20\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-22)[\\[21\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-23) and received a Bachelor of Arts degree with a [double major](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Double_major) in history and [political science](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Political_science) in 1965.[\\[22\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-ap-timeline-24)[\\[23\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-FOOTNOTETaylor199098-25)\n\n## Marriages, law school, and early career (1966–1973)\n\nMain article: [Early career of Joe Biden](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Early_life_and_career_of_Joe_Biden)\n\nSee also: [Family of Joe Biden](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Family_of_Joe_Biden)\n\nBiden married [Neilia Hunter](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neilia_Hunter_Biden), a student at [Syracuse University](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Syracuse_University), on August 27, 1966,[\\[22\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-ap-timeline-24)[\\[24\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-26) after overcoming her parents\' disinclination for her to wed a Catholic. Their wedding was held in a Catholic church in [Skaneateles, New York](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Skaneateles,_New_York_(village)).[\\[25\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-27) They had three children: [Joseph R. "Beau" Biden III](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Beau_Biden), [Robert Hunter Biden](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hunter_Biden), and Naomi Christina "Amy" Biden.[\\[22\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-ap-timeline-24)\n\nBiden earned a [Juris Doctor](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Juris_Doctor) from [Syracuse University College of Law](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Syracuse_University_College_of_Law) in 1968. In his first year of law school, he failed a course because he [plagiarized](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Plagiarism) a law review article, but the failing grade was later stricken. His grades were relatively poor, and he graduated 76th in a class of 85.[\\[26\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-nyt091887-28) He was [admitted](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Admission_to_the_bar_in_the_United_States) to the [Delaware bar](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Delaware_bar) in 1969.[\\[1\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-cong-bio-2)\n\nBiden clerked at a law firm headed by prominent local [Republican](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Republican_Party_(United_States)) William Prickett in 1968 and self-identified as a Republican.[\\[27\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-dmn-87-29)[\\[28\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-30) He disliked incumbent Democratic Delaware governor [Charles L. Terry](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Charles_L._Terry)\'s conservative racial politics and supported a more liberal Republican, [Russell W. Peterson](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Russell_W._Peterson), who defeated Terry in 1968.[\\[27\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-dmn-87-29) Local Republicans attempted to recruit Biden, but he registered as an [independent](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Independent_politician) because of his distaste for Republican presidential candidate [Richard Nixon](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Richard_Nixon).[\\[27\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-dmn-87-29)\n\n### Law practices\n\nBiden in the Syracuse 1968 yearbook\n\nIn 1969, Biden resumed practicing law, first as a [public defender](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Public_defender) in [Wilmington, Delaware](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wilmington,_Delaware). Most of his clients were [African Americans](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/African_Americans) from Wilmington\'s east side.[\\[29\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-31)[\\[30\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-32) Biden then joined a firm headed by Sid Balick, a locally active Democrat.[\\[31\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMoritz198743-33)[\\[27\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-dmn-87-29) Balick named him to the Democratic Forum, a group trying to reform and revitalize the state party,[\\[32\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWitcover201086-34) and Biden switched his registration to Democratic.[\\[27\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-dmn-87-29) He also started his own firm, Biden and Walsh.[\\[31\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMoritz198743-33) [Corporate law](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Corporate_law), however, did not appeal to him, and [criminal law](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Criminal_law) did not pay well.[\\[10\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-nyt-father-11) He supplemented his income by managing properties.[\\[33\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-watn020109-35)\n\nBiden ran for the fourth district seat on the [New Castle County Council](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/New_Castle_County,_Delaware#County_Council) in 1970 on a liberal platform that included support for public housing in the suburbs.[\\[34\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWitcover201059-36)[\\[35\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-37) Biden won the general election, defeating Republican Lawrence T. Messick, and took office on January 5, 1971.[\\[36\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-38)[\\[37\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-39) He served until January 1, 1973.[\\[38\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-40)[\\[39\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWitcover201052%E2%80%9364-41) During his time on the county council, Biden opposed large highway projects, which he argued might disrupt Wilmington neighborhoods.[\\[39\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWitcover201052%E2%80%9364-41)\n\nBiden had not openly supported or opposed the [Vietnam War](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vietnam_War) until he ran for Senate and opposed [Richard Nixon](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Richard_Nixon)\'s conduct of the war.[\\[40\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWitcover201050,_75-42) While studying at the University of Delaware and Syracuse University, Biden obtained five student [draft](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Conscription) deferments. Based on a physical examination, he was given a conditional medical deferment in 1968; in 2008, a spokesperson for Biden said his having had " [asthma](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Asthma) as a teenager" was the reason.[\\[41\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-43)\n\n### 1972 U.S. Senate campaign in Delaware\n\nMain article: [1972 United States Senate election in Delaware](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1972_United_States_Senate_election_in_Delaware)\n\nNeilia Hunter, Joe, Hunter, Naomi Christina and Beau Biden, c.\u20091972\n\nBiden defeated Republican incumbent [J. Caleb Boggs](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/J._Caleb_Boggs) to become the junior U.S. senator from Delaware in 1972. He was the only Democrat willing to challenge Boggs and, with minimal campaign funds, was thought to have no chance of winning.[\\[42\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-cby-43-44)[\\[10\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-nyt-father-11) Family members managed and staffed the campaign, which relied on meeting voters face-to-face and hand-distributing position papers,[\\[43\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-npr-72-45) an approach made feasible by Delaware\'s small size.[\\[33\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-watn020109-35) He received help from the [AFL-CIO](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/AFL-CIO) and Democratic pollster [Patrick Caddell](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Patrick_Caddell).[\\[42\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-cby-43-44) His platform focused on the environment, withdrawal from Vietnam, civil rights, mass transit, equitable taxation, health care and public dissatisfaction with "politics as usual".[\\[42\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-cby-43-44)[\\[43\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-npr-72-45) A few months before the election, Biden trailed Boggs by almost thirty percentage points,[\\[42\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-cby-43-44) but his energy, young family, and ability to connect with voters\' emotions worked to his advantage,[\\[15\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-aap08-bio-17) and he won with 50.5% of the vote.[\\[43\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-npr-72-45)\n\n### Death of first wife and daughter\n\nA few weeks after Biden was elected senator, his wife Neilia and one-year-old daughter Naomi were killed in an automobile accident in [Hockessin, Delaware](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hockessin,_Delaware), on December 18, 1972.[\\[22\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-ap-timeline-24)[\\[44\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-46) Their sons Beau (aged 3) and Hunter (aged 2) were in the car and were taken to hospital with non-life-threatening injuries.[\\[45\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWitcover201093,_98-47) He considered resigning to care for them,[\\[15\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-aap08-bio-17) but [Senate Majority Leader](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Senate_Majority_Leader) [Mike Mansfield](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mike_Mansfield) persuaded him not to.[\\[46\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-48) Biden contemplated suicide and was filled with anger and religious doubt.[\\[47\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-49)[\\[48\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-50) He wrote that he "felt God had played a horrible trick" on him[\\[49\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-51) and had trouble focusing on work.[\\[50\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-52)[\\[51\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-53)\n\n### Second marriage\n\nBiden and his second wife, [Jill](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jill_Biden), met in 1975 and married in 1977\n\nBiden met teacher [Jill Tracy Jacobs](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jill_Tracy_Jacobs) in 1975 on a [blind date](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Blind_date).[\\[52\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-54) They married at the [United Nations chapel](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Church_Center_for_the_United_Nations) in New York on June 17, 1977,[\\[53\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-55)[\\[54\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-56) and spent their honeymoon at [Lake Balaton](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lake_Balaton) in the [Hungarian People\'s Republic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hungarian_People%27s_Republic).[\\[55\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-57)[\\[56\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-58) Biden credits her with the renewal of his interest in politics and life.[\\[57\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-59)\n\nIn 1981, the couple had a daughter, [Ashley Biden](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ashley_Biden),[\\[22\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-ap-timeline-24) who is a social worker, activist, and fashion designer.[\\[58\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-60) Jill helped raise her stepsons, Hunter and Beau, who were seven and eight respectively at the time of her marriage. Hunter has worked as a Washington lobbyist and investment adviser; his business dealings, [personal life](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hunter_Biden_laptop_controversy), and [legal troubles](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Weiss_special_counsel_investigation) came under [significant scrutiny](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_House_Oversight_Committee_investigation_into_the_Biden_family) during his father\'s presidency. In December 2024, Biden pardoned Hunter following his [conviction](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Weiss_special_counsel_investigation) on gun and tax charges despite repeated promises that he would not do so.[\\[c\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-65) Beau became an Army [judge-advocate](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Judge-advocate) in Iraq and later [Delaware attorney general](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Delaware_attorney_general)[\\[63\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-66) before dying of brain cancer in 2015.[\\[64\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-67)[\\[65\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-68)\n\n### Teaching\n\nFrom 1991 to 2008, as an [adjunct professor](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Adjunct_professor), Biden co-taught a [seminar](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Seminar) on [constitutional law](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Constitutional_law) at [Widener University School of Law](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Widener_University_School_of_Law).[\\[66\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-69)[\\[67\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-70)\n\n## U.S. Senate (1973–2009)\n\nMain article: [US Senate career of Joe Biden](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/US_Senate_career_of_Joe_Biden)\n\nElected to the U.S. Senate in [1972](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1972_United_States_Senate_election_in_Delaware), Biden was reelected in [1978](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1978_United_States_Senate_election_in_Delaware), [1984](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1984_United_States_Senate_election_in_Delaware), [1990](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1990_United_States_Senate_election_in_Delaware), [1996](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1996_United_States_Senate_election_in_Delaware), [2002](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2002_United_States_Senate_election_in_Delaware), and [2008](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2008_United_States_Senate_election_in_Delaware), regularly receiving about 60% of the vote.[\\[68\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-aap08-366-71) Aged 30 when first elected, he was the [seventh-youngest senator in U.S. history](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_youngest_members_of_the_United_States_Congress#List_of_youngest_U.S._senators).[\\[69\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-72) He was junior senator to [William Roth](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/William_Roth) until Roth was defeated in 2000.[\\[70\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-73) He remains one of the [longest-serving senators](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_members_of_the_United_States_Congress_by_longevity_of_service) in U.S. history.[\\[71\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-74) For 36 years, he commuted from Washington to Wilmington via [Amtrak](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Amtrak), earning him the nickname "Amtrak Joe".[\\[72\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-75)\n\n### Senate activities\n\nBiden with President [Jimmy Carter](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jimmy_Carter), 1978Biden addresses the [September 11 attacks](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/September_11_attacks) on the Senate floor; September 12, 2001.\n\nDuring his early years in the Senate, Biden focused on consumer protection and environmental issues and called for greater government accountability.[\\[73\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-76) In 1974, he described himself as liberal on civil rights and liberties, senior citizens\' concerns, and healthcare, but conservative on other issues, including abortion and [military conscription](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Military_conscription).[\\[74\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-77) Biden was the first U.S. senator to endorse Governor [Jimmy Carter](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jimmy_Carter) for president in the [1976 Democratic primary](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1976_Democratic_Party_presidential_primaries). Carter won the Democratic nomination and the [1976 election](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1976_United_States_presidential_election).[\\[75\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-78) Biden also worked on [arms control](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arms_control).[\\[76\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-nyt-foreign-79)[\\[77\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-80) After Congress failed to ratify the [SALT II](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/SALT_II) Treaty signed in 1979 by [Soviet general secretary](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Soviet_general_secretary) [Leonid Brezhnev](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leonid_Brezhnev) and President Carter, Biden met with Soviet foreign minister [Andrei Gromyko](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Andrei_Gromyko) and secured changes that addressed the Senate Foreign Relations Committee\'s objections.[\\[78\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-81) He received considerable attention when he excoriated Secretary of State [George Shultz](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/George_Shultz) at a Senate hearing for the Reagan administration\'s support of [South Africa](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Africa) despite its policy of [apartheid](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Apartheid).[\\[27\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-dmn-87-29) In a congressional hearing in 1984, he objected to the [Strategic Defense Initiative](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Strategic_Defense_Initiative) plan to construct autonomous systems of ICBM defense.[\\[79\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-82)[\\[80\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-83) Biden was an advocate for Delaware military installations, including [Dover Air Force Base](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dover_Air_Force_Base) and [New Castle Air National Guard Base](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/New_Castle_Air_National_Guard_Base).[\\[81\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-84)\n\nIn the mid-1970s, Biden was one of the Senate\'s strongest opponents of [race-integration busing](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Race-integration_busing). His Delaware constituents strongly opposed it, and such opposition nationwide later led his party to mostly abandon school integration policies.[\\[82\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-Gadsden-85) In his first Senate campaign, Biden had expressed support for busing to remedy _de jure_ segregation, as in the South, but opposed its use to remedy _de facto_ segregation arising from racial patterns of neighborhood residency, as in Delaware; he opposed a proposed constitutional amendment banning busing entirely.[\\[83\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGadsden2012214-86) Biden supported a 1976 measure forbidding the use of federal funds for transporting students beyond the school closest to them.[\\[82\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-Gadsden-85) He co-sponsored a 1977 amendment closing loopholes in that measure, which President Carter signed into law in 1978.[\\[84\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-87)\n\nBiden shaking hands with President [Ronald Reagan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ronald_Reagan), 1984\n\nBiden became [ranking minority member](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ranking_minority_member) of the [Senate Judiciary Committee](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Senate_Judiciary_Committee) in 1981. He was a Democratic floor manager for the successful passage of the [Comprehensive Crime Control Act](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Comprehensive_Crime_Control_Act) in 1984. His supporters praised him for modifying some of the law\'s worst provisions, and it was his most important legislative accomplishment to that time.[\\[85\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-cby-44-88) In 1994, Biden helped pass the [Violent Crime Control and Law Enforcement Act](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Violent_Crime_Control_and_Law_Enforcement_Act), which included [a ban on assault weapons](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Federal_Assault_Weapons_Ban),[\\[86\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-89)[\\[87\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-90) and the [Violence Against Women Act](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Violence_Against_Women_Act),[\\[88\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-91) which he has called his most significant legislation.[\\[89\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-92) The 1994 crime law was unpopular among progressives and criticized for resulting in mass incarceration;[\\[90\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-93)[\\[91\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-94) Biden later expressed regret for passing the bill.[\\[92\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-95)\n\nBiden meeting with attorney general [Janet Reno](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Janet_Reno), 1993\n\nBiden voted for a 1993 provision that deemed homosexuality incompatible with military life, thereby banning [gay people](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_gay,_lesbian_or_bisexual_people) from serving in the armed forces.[\\[93\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-96)[\\[94\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-97) In 1996, he voted for the [Defense of Marriage Act](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Defense_of_Marriage_Act), which prohibited the federal government from recognizing same-sex marriages, thereby barring people in such marriages from equal protection under federal law and allowing states to do the same.[\\[95\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-NYT_Biden_Evolution_on_LGBTQ-98) In 2015, the act was ruled unconstitutional in _[Obergefell\xa0v. Hodges](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Obergefell_v._Hodges)_.[\\[96\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-99)\n\nBiden was critical of [Independent Counsel](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_Office_of_the_Independent_Counsel) [Ken Starr](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ken_Starr) during the 1990s [Whitewater controversy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Whitewater_controversy) and [Clinton–Lewinsky scandal](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Clinton%E2%80%93Lewinsky_scandal) investigations, saying "it\'s going to be a cold day in hell" before another independent counsel would be granted similar powers.[\\[97\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-100) He voted to acquit during the [impeachment of Bill Clinton](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Impeachment_of_Bill_Clinton).[\\[98\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-101) During the 2000s, Biden sponsored bankruptcy legislation sought by credit card issuers (such as [MBNA](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/MBNA), one of Delaware\'s largest companies).[\\[99\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-102)[\\[15\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-aap08-bio-17) [Bill Clinton](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bill_Clinton) vetoed the bill in 2000, but it passed in 2005 as the [Bankruptcy Abuse Prevention and Consumer Protection Act](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bankruptcy_Abuse_Prevention_and_Consumer_Protection_Act),[\\[15\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-aap08-bio-17) with Biden being one of only 18 Democrats to vote for it, while leading Democrats and consumer rights organizations opposed it.[\\[100\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-103) As a senator, Biden strongly supported increased [Amtrak](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Amtrak) funding and rail security.[\\[68\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-aap08-366-71)[\\[101\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-104)\n\n### Brain surgeries\n\nIn February 1988, after several episodes of severe neck pain, Biden underwent surgery to correct a leaking [intracranial berry aneurysm](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Intracranial_berry_aneurysm).[\\[102\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-105)[\\[103\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-nyt-4cmed-106) While recuperating, he suffered a [pulmonary embolism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pulmonary_embolism).[\\[103\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-nyt-4cmed-106) A second aneurysm was surgically repaired in May.[\\[103\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-nyt-4cmed-106)[\\[104\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-107) His recuperation kept him away from the Senate for seven months.[\\[105\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-108)\n\n### Senate Judiciary Committee\n\nBiden speaking at the signing of the [1994 Crime Bill](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Violent_Crime_Control_and_Law_Enforcement_Act) with President [Bill Clinton](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bill_Clinton).\n\nBiden was a longtime member of the [Senate Committee on the Judiciary](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_Senate_Committee_on_the_Judiciary). He chaired it from 1987 to 1995 and was a [ranking minority member](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ranking_member) from 1981 to 1987 and again from 1995 to 1997.[\\[106\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-109)\n\nAs chair, Biden presided over two highly contentious [U.S. Supreme Court](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Supreme_Court_of_the_United_States) confirmation hearings.[\\[15\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-aap08-bio-17) When [Robert Bork was nominated](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Robert_Bork_Supreme_Court_nomination) in 1988, Biden reversed his approval\u200d—\u200cgiven in an interview the previous year\u200d—\u200cof a hypothetical Bork nomination. Conservatives were angered,[\\[107\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBronner1989138%E2%80%93139,_214,_305-110) but at the hearings\' close Biden was praised for his fairness, humor, and courage.[\\[107\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBronner1989138%E2%80%93139,_214,_305-110)[\\[108\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-nyt-lg-87-111) Rejecting the arguments of some Bork opponents,[\\[15\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-aap08-bio-17) Biden framed his objections to Bork in terms of the conflict between Bork\'s strong [originalism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Originalism) and the view that the [U.S. Constitution](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Constitution_of_the_United_States) provides rights to liberty and privacy beyond those explicitly enumerated in its text.[\\[108\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-nyt-lg-87-111) Bork\'s nomination was rejected in the committee by a 5–9 vote[\\[108\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-nyt-lg-87-111) and then in the full Senate, 42–58.[\\[109\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-112)\n\nDuring [Clarence Thomas\'s nomination hearings](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Clarence_Thomas_Supreme_Court_nomination) in 1991, Biden\'s questions on constitutional issues were often convoluted to the point that Thomas sometimes lost track of them,[\\[110\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMayerAbramson1994213,_218,_336-113) and Thomas later wrote that Biden\'s questions were akin to " [beanballs](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Beanball)".[\\[111\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-114) After the committee hearing closed, the public learned that [Anita Hill](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Anita_Hill) had accused Thomas of [making unwelcome sexual comments](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sexual_harassment) when they had worked together.[\\[112\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-115)[\\[113\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-116) Biden had known of some of these charges, but initially shared them only with the committee because Hill was then unwilling to testify.[\\[15\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-aap08-bio-17) The committee hearing was reopened and Hill testified, but Biden did not permit testimony from other witnesses, such as a woman who had made similar charges and experts on harassment.[\\[114\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-nyt-hill-117) The full Senate confirmed Thomas by a 52–48 vote, with Biden opposed.[\\[15\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-aap08-bio-17) Liberal legal advocates and women\'s groups felt strongly that Biden had mishandled the hearings and not done enough to support Hill.[\\[114\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-nyt-hill-117) In 2019, he told Hill he regretted his treatment of her, but Hill said afterward she remained unsatisfied.[\\[115\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-118)\n\n### Senate Foreign Relations Committee\n\nSenator Biden accompanies President Clinton and other officials to [Bosnia and Herzegovina](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bosnia_and_Herzegovina), December 1997.\n\nBiden was a longtime member of the [Senate Foreign Relations Committee](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_Senate_Committee_on_Foreign_Relations). He became its ranking minority member in 1997 and chaired it from June 2001 to 2003 and 2007 to 2009.[\\[116\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-aap08-365-119) His positions were generally [liberal internationalist](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Liberal_internationalism).[\\[76\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-nyt-foreign-79)[\\[117\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-lat-foreign-120) He collaborated effectively with Republicans and sometimes went against elements of his own party.[\\[116\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-aap08-365-119)[\\[117\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-lat-foreign-120) During this time he met with at least 150 leaders from 60 countries and international organizations, becoming a well-known Democratic voice on foreign policy.[\\[118\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-121)\n\nBiden voted against authorization for the [Gulf War](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gulf_War) in 1991.[\\[117\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-lat-foreign-120) He became interested in the [Yugoslav Wars](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yugoslav_Wars) after hearing about Serbian abuses during the [Croatian War of Independence](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Croatian_War_of_Independence) in 1991.[\\[76\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-nyt-foreign-79) Once the [Bosnian War](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bosnian_War) broke out, Biden was among the first to call for the " [lift and strike](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lift_and_strike_(Bosnian_War))" policy.[\\[76\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-nyt-foreign-79)[\\[116\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-aap08-365-119) [George H. W. Bush](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/George_H._W._Bush) and [Bill Clinton](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bill_Clinton) were both reluctant to implement the policy, fearing Balkan entanglement.[\\[76\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-nyt-foreign-79)[\\[117\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-lat-foreign-120) In April 1993, Biden had a tense three-hour meeting with Serbian leader [Slobodan Milošević](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Slobodan_Milo%C5%A1evi%C4%87).[\\[119\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-wapo-bosnia-122) Biden worked on several versions of legislative language urging the U.S. toward greater involvement.[\\[119\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-wapo-bosnia-122) He has called his role in affecting Balkan policy in the mid-1990s his "proudest moment in public life" related to foreign policy.[\\[117\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-lat-foreign-120) In 1999, during the [Kosovo War](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kosovo_War), Biden supported the [NATO bombing of Yugoslavia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/NATO_bombing_of_Yugoslavia).[\\[76\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-nyt-foreign-79) He and Senator [John McCain](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_McCain) co-sponsored the McCain-Biden Kosovo Resolution, which called on Clinton to use all necessary force, including ground troops, to confront Milošević over Yugoslav actions toward [Kosovo Albanians](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kosovo_Albanians).[\\[117\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-lat-foreign-120)[\\[120\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-wsj082508-123)\n\n#### Wars in Afghanistan and Iraq\n\nMain article: [War on terror](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/War_on_terror)\n\nBiden addresses the press after meeting with Prime Minister [Ayad Allawi](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ayad_Allawi) in [Baghdad](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Baghdad) in 2004.\n\nBiden was a strong supporter of the [War in Afghanistan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/War_in_Afghanistan_(2001%E2%80%932021)), saying, "Whatever it takes, we should do it."[\\[121\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-124) As head of the Senate Foreign Relations Committee, he said in 2002 that Iraqi president [Saddam Hussein](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Saddam_Hussein) was a threat to national security and there was no other option than to "eliminate" that threat.[\\[122\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-125) In October 2002, he voted in favor of the [Authorization for Use of Military Force Against Iraq](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authorization_for_Use_of_Military_Force_Against_Iraq), approving the [U.S. invasion of Iraq](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/U.S._invasion_of_Iraq).[\\[117\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-lat-foreign-120) As chair of the committee, he assembled witnesses to testify in favor of the authorization. They gave testimony grossly misrepresenting the intent, history, and status of Saddam and his government, and touted Iraq\'s fictional possession of [weapons of mass destruction](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Weapons_of_mass_destruction).[\\[123\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-126) Biden eventually became a critic of the war, calling his vote a "mistake" by 2005,[\\[124\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-127)[\\[125\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-128) but did not push for withdrawal.[\\[117\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-lat-foreign-120)[\\[119\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-wapo-bosnia-122) He supported the appropriations for the occupation, but argued that the war should be internationalized, that more soldiers were needed, and that the Bush administration should "level with the [American people](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Americans)" about its cost and length.[\\[116\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-aap08-365-119)[\\[120\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-wsj082508-123)\n\nBy late 2006, Biden\'s stance had shifted considerably. He opposed the [troop surge of 2007](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Troop_surge_of_2007),[\\[117\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-lat-foreign-120)[\\[119\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-wapo-bosnia-122) saying General [David Petraeus](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/David_Petraeus) was "dead, flat wrong" in believing the surge could work.[\\[126\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-nytm-traub-129) Biden, through a plan developed with [Council on Foreign Relations](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Council_on_Foreign_Relations) president [Leslie H. Gelb](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leslie_H._Gelb), instead advocated dividing Iraq into a loose [federation of three ethnic states](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Federalism_in_Iraq).[\\[d\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-134) In September 2007, a non-binding resolution endorsing the plan passed the Senate,[\\[131\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-135) but the idea failed to gain traction.[\\[126\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-nytm-traub-129)\n\n## 1988 and 2008 presidential campaigns\n\n### 1988 campaign\n\nMain article: [Joe Biden 1988 presidential campaign](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Joe_Biden_1988_presidential_campaign)\n\nBiden speaks at a campaign event, 1987.\n\nBiden declared his candidacy for the [1988 Democratic presidential nomination](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1988_Democratic_Party_presidential_primaries) on June 9, 1987.[\\[132\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-136) He was considered a strong candidate because of his moderate image, his speaking ability, his high profile as chair of the Senate Judiciary Committee at the upcoming [Robert Bork Supreme Court nomination](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Robert_Bork_Supreme_Court_nomination) hearings, and his appeal to [Baby Boomers](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Baby_Boomer).[\\[27\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-dmn-87-29)[\\[133\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-nyt083187-137)[\\[134\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-FOOTNOTETaylor199083-138) He raised more in the first quarter of 1987 than any other candidate.[\\[133\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-nyt083187-137)[\\[134\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-FOOTNOTETaylor199083-138)\n\nBy August, Biden\'s campaign messaging had become confused due to staff rivalries,[\\[135\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-FOOTNOTETaylor1990108%E2%80%93109-139) and in September, he was accused of plagiarizing a speech by [British Labour Party](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Labour_Party_(UK)) leader [Neil Kinnock](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neil_Kinnock).[\\[136\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-140) Biden had credited Kinnock on previous occasions,[\\[137\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-141)[\\[138\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-lat-speech-142) but did not on two occasions in August.[\\[139\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-143):\u200a230–232\u200a[\\[138\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-lat-speech-142) Earlier that year, Biden had also used passages from a speech by [Robert F. Kennedy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Robert_F._Kennedy) (for which his aides took blame) and the [inaugural address of John F. Kennedy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Inaugural_address_of_John_F._Kennedy). Two years earlier he had used a 1976 passage by [Hubert Humphrey](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hubert_Humphrey).[\\[140\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-144) Biden responded that politicians often borrow from one another without giving credit, and that one of his rivals for the nomination, [Jesse Jackson](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jesse_Jackson), had called him to point out that Jackson had used the same material by Humphrey that Biden had used.[\\[15\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-aap08-bio-17)[\\[26\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-nyt091887-28) A few days later, it was publicized that, while in law school, Biden had taken text from a _[Fordham Law Review](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fordham_Law_Review)_ article with inadequate citations.[\\[26\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-nyt091887-28) At Biden\'s request the Delaware Supreme Court\'s Board of Professional Responsibility reviewed the incident and concluded that he had violated no rules.[\\[141\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-145)\n\nBiden has made several false or exaggerated claims about his early life: that he had earned three degrees in college, that he attended [law school](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Law_school) on a full scholarship, that he had graduated in the top half of his class,[\\[142\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-146)[\\[143\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-147) and that he had marched in the [civil rights movement](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Civil_rights_movement).[\\[144\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-148) The limited amount of other news about the presidential race amplified these disclosures,[\\[145\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-149) and on September 23, 1987, Biden withdrew his candidacy.[\\[146\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-150)\n\n### 2008 campaign\n\nMain article: [Joe Biden 2008 presidential campaign](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Joe_Biden_2008_presidential_campaign)\n\nBiden campaigns at a house party in [Creston, Iowa](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Creston,_Iowa), July 2007.\n\nAfter exploring running in several previous cycles, in January 2007, Biden declared [his candidacy in the 2008 elections](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2008_Democratic_Party_presidential_primaries).[\\[68\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-aap08-366-71)[\\[147\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-151)[\\[148\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-152) Biden focused on the [Iraq War](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iraq_War), his record as chairman of major Senate committees, and his foreign-policy experience.[\\[149\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-153) Biden was noted for his [one-liners](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/One-line_joke) during the campaign; in one debate he said of Republican candidate [Rudy Giuliani](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rudy_Giuliani), "There\'s only three things he mentions in a sentence: a noun, and a verb and [9/11](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cultural_influence_of_the_September_11_attacks)."[\\[150\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-154)\n\nBiden had difficulty raising funds, struggled to draw people to his rallies, and failed to gain traction against the high-profile candidacies of [Barack Obama](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama) and [Hillary Clinton](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hillary_Clinton).[\\[151\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-155) He never rose above single digits in [national polls of the Democratic candidates](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nationwide_opinion_polling_for_the_Democratic_Party_2008_presidential_candidates). In the first contest on January 3, 2008, Biden placed fifth in the [Iowa caucuses](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iowa_Democratic_caucuses,_2008), garnering slightly less than one percent of the state delegates.[\\[152\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-156) He withdrew from the race that evening.[\\[153\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-157)\n\nDespite its lack of success, Biden\'s 2008 campaign raised his stature in the political world.[\\[154\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-gamechange-158):\u200a336\u200a In particular, it changed the relationship between Biden and Obama. Although they had served together on the [Senate Foreign Relations Committee](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Senate_Foreign_Relations_Committee), they had not been close: Biden resented Obama\'s quick rise to political stardom,[\\[126\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-nytm-traub-129)[\\[155\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWolffe2009218-159) while Obama viewed Biden as garrulous and patronizing.[\\[154\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-gamechange-158):\u200a28,\u200a337–338\u200a Having gotten to know each other during 2007, Obama appreciated Biden\'s campaign style and appeal to working-class voters, and Biden said he became convinced Obama was "the real deal".[\\[155\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWolffe2009218-159)[\\[154\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-gamechange-158):\u200a28,\u200a337–338\n\n## 2008 and 2012 vice presidential campaigns\n\n### 2008 campaign\n\nMain articles: [Barack Obama 2008 presidential campaign](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama_2008_presidential_campaign) and [2008 Democratic Party vice presidential candidate selection](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2008_Democratic_Party_vice_presidential_candidate_selection)\n\nBiden speaks at the August 23, 2008, vice presidential announcement at the [Old State Capitol](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Old_State_Capitol_State_Historic_Site) in [Springfield, Illinois](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Springfield,_Illinois).\n\nIn August 2008, Obama and Biden met in secret to discuss the possibility of a place for Biden in the Obama administration,[\\[156\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-ny-lizza-160) and developed a strong personal rapport.[\\[155\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWolffe2009218-159) On August 22, Obama announced that Biden would be his [running mate](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Running_mate).[\\[157\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-161) _[The New York Times](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_New_York_Times)_ reported that the choice reflected a desire for someone with [foreign policy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Foreign_policy) and [national security](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/National_security) experience.[\\[158\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-162) Others pointed out Biden\'s appeal to middle-class and [blue-collar](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Blue-collar) voters.[\\[159\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-163)[\\[160\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWolffe2009217-164) Biden was officially nominated for vice president on August 27 at the [2008 Democratic National Convention](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2008_Democratic_National_Convention) in [Denver](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Denver).[\\[161\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-165)\n\nBiden\'s vice-presidential campaigning gained little media attention, as the press devoted far more coverage to the Republican nominee and then- [governor of Alaska](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Governor_of_Alaska), [Sarah Palin](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sarah_Palin).[\\[162\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-nyt-no2-166)[\\[163\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-167) Under instructions from the campaign, Biden kept his speeches succinct and tried to avoid offhand remarks.[\\[164\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-168)[\\[165\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-169) Privately, Biden\'s remarks frustrated Obama. "How many times is Biden gonna say something stupid?", he once angrily asked.[\\[154\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-gamechange-158):\u200a411–414,\u200a419\u200a Obama campaign staffers called Biden\'s blunders "Joe bombs" and kept Biden uninformed about strategy discussions, which irked Biden.[\\[166\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-nyt0508122-170) Relations between the two campaigns became strained for a month, until Biden apologized to Obama and the two built a stronger partnership.[\\[154\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-gamechange-158):\u200a411–414\n\nAs the [2008 financial crisis](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2008_financial_crisis) reached a peak in September 2008, and the proposed [Emergency Economic Stabilization Act of 2008](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Emergency_Economic_Stabilization_Act_of_2008) became a major factor in the campaign, Biden voted for the $700 billion [Emergency Economic Stabilization Act of 2008](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Emergency_Economic_Stabilization_Act_of_2008), which passed in the Senate.[\\[167\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-171) On October 2, he participated in the [vice-presidential debate](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2008_United_States_presidential_debates) with Palin at [Washington University in St. Louis](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Washington_University_in_St._Louis). Post-debate polls found that while Palin exceeded many voters\' expectations, Biden had still won the debate overall.[\\[168\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWitcover2010655%E2%80%93661-172) On November 4, Obama and Biden [were elected](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2008_United_States_presidential_election).[\\[169\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-173)[\\[170\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-174)[\\[171\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-175)\n\nAs Biden was running for vice president, he was also running for reelection to the Senate,[\\[172\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-176) as permitted by Delaware law.[\\[68\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-aap08-366-71) Having been [reelected](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2008_United_States_Senate_election_in_Delaware) to the Senate as well as the vice presidency,[\\[173\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-177) Biden made a point of not resigning from the Senate before he was sworn in for his seventh term in January 2009.[\\[174\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-178) He [resigned from the Senate](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Resignation_from_the_United_States_Senate) on January 15.[\\[175\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-179)[\\[176\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-180)\n\n### 2012 campaign\n\nMain article: [Barack Obama 2012 presidential campaign](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama_2012_presidential_campaign)\n\nObama watching Biden debate Paul Ryan in the vice-presidential debate on [Air Force One](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Air_Force_One)\n\nIn October 2010, Biden said Obama had asked him to remain as his running mate for the [2012 presidential election](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_United_States_presidential_election),[\\[177\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-nyt1013102-181) but with Obama\'s popularity declining, [White House Chief of Staff](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/White_House_Chief_of_Staff) [William M. Daley](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/William_M._Daley) conducted some secret polling and focus group research in late 2011 on the idea of replacing Biden with Hillary Clinton.[\\[178\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-nyt-dd-replace-182) The notion was dropped when the results showed no appreciable improvement,[\\[178\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-nyt-dd-replace-182) and White House officials later said Obama himself never entertained the idea.[\\[179\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-183)\n\nBiden\'s May 2012 statement that he was "absolutely comfortable" with [same-sex marriage](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Same-sex_marriage) gained considerable public attention in comparison to Obama\'s position, which had been described as "evolving".[\\[180\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-184) Biden made his statement without administration consent, and Obama and his aides were irked, since Obama had planned to shift position in the build-up to the party convention.[\\[166\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-nyt0508122-170)[\\[181\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-ap051012-185)[\\[182\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-186) Gay rights advocates seized upon Biden\'s statement,[\\[181\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-ap051012-185) and within days, Obama announced that he too supported same-sex marriage, an action in part forced by Biden\'s remarks.[\\[183\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-187)\n\nBiden had a heavy schedule of appearances in swing states as the reelection campaign began in earnest in spring 2012.[\\[184\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-time-be-joe-188)[\\[185\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-time-mo-189) An August 2012 remark before a mixed-race audience that Republican proposals to relax Wall Street regulations would "put y\'all back in chains" again drew attention to Biden\'s propensity for colorful remarks.[\\[184\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-time-be-joe-188)[\\[186\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-190)[\\[187\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-191)\n\nFollowing the first presidential debate of the general election, in which Obama\'s performance was considered surprisingly lackluster,[\\[188\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-192) his lead over Romney collapsed,[\\[189\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-193) putting pressure on Biden to stop the bleeding with a strong showing against the Republican vice-presidential nominee, [Paul Ryan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Paul_Ryan).[\\[190\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-194)[\\[191\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-195) Some political analysts considered Biden\'s performance in the October 11 vice-presidential debate one of the best of his career[\\[192\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-196)[\\[193\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-197) and a key factor in Obama\'s rebound in the polls and eventual victory.[\\[194\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-198)[\\[195\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-199) The debate also became memorable for the popularization of Biden\'s use of the phrase "a bunch of malarkey" in response to an attack by Ryan on the administration\'s response to the [attacks on the U.S. embassy in Benghazi](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Benghazi_attack) in September.[\\[196\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-200)[\\[197\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-201) Biden reused the phrase during his 2020 presidential campaign.[\\[198\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-202) On November 6, Obama and Biden were reelected.[\\[199\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-203)\n\n## Vice presidency (2009–2017)\n\nMain article: [Vice presidency of Joe Biden](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vice_presidency_of_Joe_Biden)\n\nSee also: [Presidency of Barack Obama](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Presidency_of_Barack_Obama)\n\n### First term (2009–2013)\n\nSee also: [First inauguration of Barack Obama](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/First_inauguration_of_Barack_Obama)\n\nBiden being sworn in as vice president by Supreme Court Justice [John Paul Stevens](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_Paul_Stevens) on January 20, 2009\n\nBiden said he intended to eliminate some explicit roles assumed by [George W. Bush](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/George_W._Bush)\'s vice president, [Dick Cheney](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dick_Cheney), and did not intend to emulate any previous vice presidency.[\\[200\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-204) He was sworn in on January 20, 2009.[\\[201\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-205) He was the first vice president from [Delaware](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Delaware)[\\[202\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-206) and the first [Roman Catholic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Roman_Catholic) vice president.[\\[203\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-207)[\\[204\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-208) Members of the Obama administration said Biden\'s role in the White House was to be a contrarian and force others to defend their positions.[\\[205\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-The_New_York_Times-2-209) White House chief of staff [Rahm Emanuel](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rahm_Emanuel) said Biden helped counter [groupthink](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Groupthink).[\\[206\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-nyt032809-210) The Bidens maintained a relaxed atmosphere at their [official residence](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Number_One_Observatory_Circle) in Washington, often entertaining their grandchildren, and regularly returned to their home in Delaware.[\\[207\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-211)\n\nBiden\'s official portrait as vice president, 2009\n\nBiden oversaw [infrastructure spending from the Obama stimulus package](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/American_Recovery_and_Reinvestment_Act_of_2009#Infrastructure_investment) intended to help counteract the [ongoing recession](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Late-2000s_recession).[\\[208\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-212) Confronted with rising unemployment through July 2009, Biden
