acknowledged that the administration had "misread how bad the economy was", but maintained confidence the stimulus package would create many more jobs once the pace of expenditures picked up.[\\[209\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-213) When he completed that role in February 2011, he said the number of fraud incidents with stimulus monies had been less than one percent.[\\[210\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-214)\n\nBiden\'s off-message response to a question in April 2009, during the beginning of the [swine flu outbreak](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2009_flu_pandemic), led to a swift retraction by the White House.[\\[211\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-215) The remark revived Biden\'s reputation for [gaffes](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Political_gaffe).[\\[212\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-216)[\\[213\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-nw-cov-1010092-217)[\\[214\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-218) A [hot mic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hot_mic) picked up Biden telling Obama that his signing the [Patient Protection and Affordable Care Act](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Patient_Protection_and_Affordable_Care_Act) was "a big fucking deal" on March 23, 2010.[\\[215\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-219) Despite their different personalities, Obama and Biden formed a friendship, partly based around Obama\'s daughter Sasha and Biden\'s granddaughter Maisy, who attended [Sidwell Friends School](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sidwell_Friends_School) together.[\\[166\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-nyt0508122-170)\n\nBiden visited [Kosovo](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kosovo) in May 2009 and affirmed the U.S. position that its "independence is irreversible".[\\[216\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-220) He lost an internal debate to Secretary of State [Hillary Clinton](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hillary_Clinton) about [sending 21,000 new troops to Afghanistan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/War_in_Afghanistan_(2001%E2%80%932021)),[\\[217\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-221)[\\[218\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-222) but his skepticism was valued,[\\[219\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-pol091609-223) and his views gained more influence as Obama reconsidered his Afghanistan strategy.[\\[213\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-nw-cov-1010092-217) Obama delegated Biden to oversee Iraq policy, and he became the administration\'s point man in delivering messages to Iraqi leadership before the exit of U.S. troops in 2011.[\\[e\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-226)\n\nPresident Obama congratulates Biden for his role in shaping the [debt ceiling](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_debt_ceiling) deal which led to the [Budget Control Act of 2011](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Budget_Control_Act_of_2011).\n\nBiden campaigned heavily for Democrats in the [2010 midterm elections](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_elections,_2010), maintaining an attitude of optimism in the face of predictions of large-scale losses for the party.[\\[177\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-nyt1013102-181) After big Republican gains in the elections and Emanuel\'s departure, Biden\'s past relationships with Republicans in Congress became more important.[\\[222\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-pol1209102-227)[\\[223\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-nyt1211102-228) He led the successful administration effort to gain Senate approval for the [New START treaty](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/New_START_treaty).[\\[222\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-pol1209102-227)[\\[223\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-nyt1211102-228) In December 2010, Biden\'s advocacy for a middle ground, followed by his negotiations with Senate minority leader [Mitch McConnell](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mitch_McConnell), were instrumental in producing the administration\'s compromise tax package that included a temporary [extension of the Bush tax cuts](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Extension_of_the_Bush_tax_cuts).[\\[223\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-nyt1211102-228)[\\[224\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-229) The package passed as the [Tax Relief, Unemployment Insurance Reauthorization, and Job Creation Act of 2010](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tax_Relief,_Unemployment_Insurance_Reauthorization,_and_Job_Creation_Act_of_2010).\n\nBiden, Obama and the national security team gathered in the [White House Situation Room](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/White_House_Situation_Room) to monitor the progress of the May 2011 [mission](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Killing_of_Osama_bin_Laden) to kill [Osama bin Laden](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Osama_bin_Laden).\n\nObama delegated Biden to lead negotiations with Congress during the [2011 U.S. debt ceiling crisis](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_debt-ceiling_crisis_of_2011).[\\[225\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-230) Biden\'s relationship with McConnell brought about the [Budget Control Act of 2011](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Budget_Control_Act_of_2011) that solved the crisis.[\\[226\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-231)[\\[227\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-232)[\\[228\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-233) Some reports suggest that Biden opposed proceeding with the May 2011 [U.S. mission to kill Osama bin Laden](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/U.S._mission_to_kill_Osama_bin_Laden),[\\[185\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-time-mo-189)[\\[229\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-234) lest failure adversely affect Obama\'s reelection prospects.[\\[230\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-235)[\\[231\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-236) In 2012, Biden made the case for Obama\'s reelection: "Osama bin Laden is dead and General Motors is alive."[\\[232\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-237)\n\nObama named Biden to head the [Gun Violence Task Force](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gun_Violence_Task_Force), created to address the causes of [school shootings](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/School_shooting) and consider possible [gun control](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gun_control) measures in the aftermath of the [Sandy Hook Elementary School shooting](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sandy_Hook_Elementary_School_shooting), in December 2012.[\\[233\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-238) Later that month, during the final days before the United States fell off the " [fiscal cliff](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_fiscal_cliff)", Biden\'s relationship with McConnell again proved important as the two negotiated a deal that led to the [American Taxpayer Relief Act of 2012](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/American_Taxpayer_Relief_Act_of_2012) being passed at the start of 2013.[\\[234\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-239)[\\[235\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-ap-cliff-240)\n\n### Second term (2013–2017)\n\nSee also: [Second inauguration of Barack Obama](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Second_inauguration_of_Barack_Obama)\n\nBiden\'s official portrait as vice president, 2013\n\nBiden was inaugurated to a second term on January 20, 2013, at a small ceremony at [Number One Observatory Circle](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Number_One_Observatory_Circle), his official residence, with Justice [Sonia Sotomayor](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sonia_Sotomayor) presiding (a public ceremony took place on January 21).[\\[236\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-241) He played little part in discussions that led to the October 2013 passage of the [Continuing Appropriations Act, 2014](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Continuing_Appropriations_Act,_2014), which resolved the [federal government shutdown of 2013](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2013_United_States_federal_government_shutdown) and the [debt-ceiling crisis of 2013](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_debt-ceiling_crisis_of_2013). Senate Majority Leader [Harry Reid](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harry_Reid) and other Democratic leaders cut him out of direct talks with Congress, feeling Biden had given too much away during previous negotiations.[\\[237\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-242)[\\[238\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-243)[\\[239\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-244)\n\nBiden\'s Violence Against Women Act was reauthorized again in 2013. The act led to related developments, such as the [White House Council on Women and Girls](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/White_House_Council_on_Women_and_Girls), begun in the first term, as well as the [White House Task Force to Protect Students from Sexual Assault](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/White_House_Task_Force_to_Protect_Students_from_Sexual_Assault), begun in January 2014 with Biden and [Valerie Jarrett](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Valerie_Jarrett) as co-chairs.[\\[240\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-245)[\\[241\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-246) He talked about sexual violence while introducing [Lady Gaga](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lady_Gaga) at the [88th Academy Awards](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/88th_Academy_Awards) in 2016, receiving a [standing ovation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Standing_ovation) from the audience.[\\[242\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-247)\n\nBiden receiving the [Presidential Medal of Freedom](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Presidential_Medal_of_Freedom) on January 12, 2017, four years prior to his presidential inauguration in 2021, the first U.S. president to do so.\n\nBiden favored arming [Syria\'s rebel fighters](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timber_Sycamore).[\\[243\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-248) As the [ISIL](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/ISIL) [insurgency in Iraq](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/War_in_Iraq_(2013%E2%80%932017)) intensified in 2014, renewed attention was paid to the Biden-Gelb Iraqi federalization plan of 2006, with some observers suggesting Biden had been right all along.[\\[244\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-249)[\\[245\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-250) He had close relationships with several Latin American leaders and visited the region 16 times during his vice presidency, the most of any president or vice president.[\\[246\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-251) In August 2016, Biden visited [Serbia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Serbia), where he met with the Serbian Prime Minister [Aleksandar Vučić](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Aleksandar_Vu%C4%8Di%C4%87) and expressed condolences for civilian victims of the bombing campaign during the Kosovo War.[\\[247\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-252) Biden never [cast a tie-breaking vote in the Senate](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_tie-breaking_votes_cast_by_vice_presidents_of_the_United_States), making him the longest-serving vice president with this distinction.[\\[248\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-253)\n\nDuring his second term, Biden was often said to be preparing for a bid for the [2016 Democratic presidential nomination](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2016_Democratic_Party_presidential_primaries).[\\[249\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-Itkowitz1-254) With his family, friends, and donors encouraging him in mid-2015 to enter the race, and with [Hillary Clinton](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hillary_Clinton)\'s favorability ratings in decline at that time, Biden was reported to be seriously considering the prospect and a " [Draft](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Draft_(politics)) Biden 2016" [Political action committee](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Political_action_committee) (PAC) was established.[\\[249\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-Itkowitz1-254)[\\[250\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-255)[\\[251\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-256) During 2015, Biden was uncertain about running, particularly due to the recent death of his son Beau,[\\[252\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-257) before ultimately announcing his decision not to run that October.[\\[253\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-258)[\\[254\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-259)[\\[255\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-260)\n\n## Post-vice presidency (2017–2021)\n\nBiden attending the [state funeral of George H. W. Bush](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Death_and_state_funeral_of_George_H._W._Bush) in December 2018\n\nBiden left office on January 20, 2017, and was succeeded by the 48th [vice president of the United States](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vice_President_of_the_United_States), [Mike Pence](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mike_Pence). After leaving the vice presidency, Biden became an honorary professor at the [University of Pennsylvania](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/University_of_Pennsylvania), developing the [Penn Biden Center for Diplomacy and Global Engagement](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Penn_Biden_Center_for_Diplomacy_and_Global_Engagement). Biden remained in that position until 2019.[\\[256\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-261)[\\[257\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-262)\n\nIn 2017, Biden wrote a memoir, _[Promise Me, Dad](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Promise_Me,_Dad)_, and went on a book tour.[\\[258\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-263) By 2019, he and his wife reported that they had earned over $15 million since the end of his vice presidency from speaking engagements and book sales.[\\[259\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-264)\n\nBiden remained in the public eye, endorsing candidates while continuing to comment on politics, climate change, and the [presidency of Donald Trump](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/First_presidency_of_Donald_Trump).[\\[260\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-265)[\\[261\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-foreign-policy2-266)[\\[262\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-267) He also continued to speak out in favor of LGBT rights, continuing advocacy on an issue he had become more closely associated with during his vice presidency.[\\[263\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-268)[\\[264\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-269) In 2018, he gave a eulogy for Senator [John McCain](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_McCain).[\\[265\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-270) Biden continued to support [cancer research](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cancer_research).[\\[266\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-271)\n\n## 2020 presidential campaign\n\nMain article: [Joe Biden 2020 presidential campaign](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Joe_Biden_2020_presidential_campaign)\n\n### Speculation and announcement\n\nBiden at his presidential kickoff rally in [Philadelphia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Philadelphia), May 2019\n\nBetween 2016 and 2019, media outlets often mentioned Biden as a likely candidate for president in 2020.[\\[267\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-272) When asked if he would run, he gave varied and ambivalent answers, saying "never say never".[\\[268\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-273) A [political action committee](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Political_action_committee) known as [Time for Biden](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Time_for_Biden) was formed in January 2018.[\\[269\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-274) Biden launched his campaign on April 25, 2019,[\\[270\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-275) saying he was worried by the [Trump administration](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/First_presidency_of_Donald_Trump) and felt a "sense of duty".[\\[271\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-276)\n\n### Campaign\n\nFurther information: [2020 Democratic Party presidential primaries](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2020_Democratic_Party_presidential_primaries) and [2020 United States presidential debates](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2020_United_States_presidential_debates)\n\nPublic polling showed Biden as one of the best-performing Democratic candidates head-to-head against Trump.[\\[272\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-277)[\\[273\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-278)[\\[274\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-279) With Democrats keenly focused on "electability" for defeating Trump,[\\[275\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-280) this boosted his popularity among Democratic voters.[\\[276\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-281) It also made Biden a frequent target of Trump.[\\[277\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-282)[\\[278\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-283) In September 2019, it was reported that Trump had pressured Ukrainian president [Volodymyr Zelenskyy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Volodymyr_Zelenskyy) to investigate [alleged wrongdoing](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Biden%E2%80%93Ukraine_conspiracy_theory) by Biden and his son [Hunter Biden](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hunter_Biden).[\\[279\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-284) No evidence was produced of any wrongdoing by the Bidens.[\\[280\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-285)[\\[281\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-286)[\\[282\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-287) Trump was perceived by many as attempting to hurt Biden\'s chances of winning the presidency,[\\[283\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-288) resulting in [a political scandal](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Trump%E2%80%93Ukraine_scandal)[\\[284\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-289) and [Trump\'s impeachment](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/First_impeachment_of_Donald_Trump).[\\[285\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-290)\n\nIn March 2019 and April 2019, eight women accused Biden of inappropriate physical contact, such as embracing, touching or kissing.[\\[286\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-291) Biden had previously called himself a "tactile politician" and admitted this behavior had caused trouble for him.[\\[287\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-292) Journalist [Mark Bowden](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mark_Bowden) described Biden\'s lifelong habit of talking close, writing that he "doesn\'t just meet you, he engulfs you... scooting closer" and leaning forward to talk.[\\[288\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-The_Atlantic-293) In April 2019, Biden pledged to be more "respectful of people\'s personal space".[\\[289\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-294)\n\nBiden at a rally on the eve of the Iowa caucuses, February 2020\n\nThroughout 2019, Biden stayed generally ahead of other Democrats in national polls.[\\[290\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-295)[\\[291\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-296) Despite this, he finished fourth in the [Iowa caucuses](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2020_Iowa_caucuses) and fifth in the [New Hampshire primary](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/New_Hampshire_presidential_primary).[\\[292\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-297)[\\[293\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-298) He performed better in the [Nevada caucuses](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nevada_presidential_caucuses), reaching the 15% required for delegates, but still finished 21.6 percentage points behind [Bernie Sanders](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bernie_Sanders_2020_presidential_campaign).[\\[294\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-299) Making strong appeals to Black voters on the campaign trail and in the South Carolina debate, Biden won the [South Carolina primary](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2020_South_Carolina_Democratic_primary) by more than 28 points.[\\[295\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-300) After the withdrawals and subsequent endorsements of candidates [Pete Buttigieg](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pete_Buttigieg) and [Amy Klobuchar](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Amy_Klobuchar), he made large gains in the [Super Tuesday](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Super_Tuesday) primaries. Biden won [18 of the next 26 contests](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Results_of_the_2020_Democratic_Party_presidential_primaries), putting him in the lead.[\\[296\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-301) [Elizabeth Warren](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Elizabeth_Warren) and [Michael Bloomberg](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Michael_Bloomberg) soon dropped out, and Biden expanded his lead with victories over Sanders in four states on March 10.[\\[297\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-302) In March 2019, Biden said, "I view myself as a bridge, not as anything else. There\'s an entire generation of leaders you saw stand behind me. They are the future of this country."[\\[298\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-303)\n\nIn late March 2020, Tara Reade, one of the eight women who in 2019 had accused Biden of inappropriate physical contact, [accused](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Joe_Biden_sexual_assault_allegation) Biden of having sexually assaulted her in 1993.[\\[299\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-nytimesallegations-304) There were inconsistencies between Reade\'s 2019 and 2020 allegations.[\\[299\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-nytimesallegations-304)[\\[300\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-305) Biden and his campaign denied the sexual assault allegation.[\\[301\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-306)[\\[302\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-307)\n\nWhen Sanders suspended his campaign on April 8, 2020, Biden became the Democratic Party\'s [presumptive nominee](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Presumptive_nominee).[\\[303\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-308) On April 13, Sanders endorsed Biden.[\\[304\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-309) [Barack Obama](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama) endorsed Biden the next day.[\\[305\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-310) There was a great deal of interest in who his running mate would be, in part because of "the expectation, downplayed but not exactly denied by the Biden campaign, that the 77-year-old would be a one-term president".[\\[306\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-NYT-311) Biden said, "I view myself as a transition candidate."[\\[306\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-NYT-311) On August 11, Biden announced [Kamala Harris](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kamala_Harris) as his running mate, making her the first African American and first [South Asian American](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Asian_American) vice-presidential nominee on a major-party ticket.[\\[307\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-312) On August 18, at the [2020 Democratic National Convention](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2020_Democratic_National_Convention), Biden officially became the Democratic Party nominee for president in the [2020 election](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2020_United_States_presidential_election).[\\[308\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-313)[\\[309\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-314)\n\n### Presidential election and transition\n\nMain articles: [2020 United States presidential election](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2020_United_States_presidential_election) and [Presidential transition of Joe Biden](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Presidential_transition_of_Joe_Biden)\n\n2020 electoral vote results. Biden won 306–232.\n\nBiden was [elected](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2020_United_States_presidential_election) the 46th president in November 2020, defeating the incumbent, [Donald Trump](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump).[\\[310\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-315) Trump and numerous other Republicans repeatedly made [false claims](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/False_or_misleading_statements_by_Donald_Trump) that widespread [electoral fraud](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Electoral_fraud) had occurred and that only he had legitimately won the election.[\\[f\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-TrumpMakesClaimsOfElectionFraud-318) Biden\'s transition was delayed by several weeks as the White House ordered federal agencies not to cooperate.[\\[313\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-319) On November 23, [General Services Administrator](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/General_Services_Administration) [Emily W. Murphy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Emily_W._Murphy) formally recognized Biden as the apparent winner of the 2020 election and authorized the start of a transition process to the Biden administration.[\\[314\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-320)\n\nAlthough most resulting lawsuits were either dismissed or ruled against by numerous courts,[\\[g\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-CourtsDismissClaimsOfElectionFraud-327) Trump nonetheless [conspired](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Criminal_conspiracy)[\\[311\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-JackSmithReportVol1-316):\u200a33–53\u200a with his [campaign](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump_2020_presidential_campaign) team to [submit documents in several states](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Trump_fake_electors_plot) (all of which Biden had won) that [falsely claimed](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Making_false_statements) to be legitimate electoral votes for President Trump and Vice President [Mike Pence](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mike_Pence).[\\[h\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-TrumpFakeElectors-331) After the submission of these documents, the Trump campaign intended that the [presiding officer of the United States Senate](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Presiding_Officer_of_the_United_States_Senate), either [President of the Senate](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/President_of_the_Senate_of_the_United_States) Pence or [President pro tempore](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/President_pro_tempore_of_the_United_States_Senate) [Chuck Grassley](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chuck_Grassley), would claim the unilateral power to reject [electors](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_Electoral_College#Electors) during the [January 6, 2021, vote counting session](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2021_United_States_Electoral_College_vote_count); the presiding officer would reject all electors from the several states for which the Trump campaign had submitted false documents, leaving 232 votes for Trump and 222 votes for Biden, thereby [overturning the election results](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Attempts_to_overturn_the_2020_United_States_presidential_election) in Trump\'s favor.[\\[i\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-UnilateralRejectionOfElectors-338) This plan failed after Pence refused to cooperate with it.[\\[j\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-PenceRefusesToRejectElectors-341) Trump nevertheless urged his supporters on January 6 to march to the [Capitol](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_Capitol) while the joint session of Congress was assembled there to count electoral votes and formalize Biden\'s victory, whereupon [hundreds of people stormed](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/January_6_United_States_Capitol_attack) the building and interrupted the count. During the attack, Biden addressed the nation, calling the events "an unprecedented assault unlike anything we\'ve seen in modern times".[\\[332\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-342)[\\[333\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-343) After the Capitol was cleared, Congress officially counted the election results, with Pence, in his role as president of the Senate, announcing Biden and Harris as the winners.[\\[334\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-344) On January 7, Trump acknowledged the incoming administration without mentioning Biden\'s name.[\\[335\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-345)\n\n## Presidency (2021–2025)\n\nMain article: [Presidency of Joe Biden](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Presidency_of_Joe_Biden)\n\n| Part of [a series](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Category:Liberalism_in_the_United_States) on |\n| [Liberalismin the United States](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Liberalism_in_the_United_States) |\n| Schools - _[The Problem with Jon Stewart](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Problem_with_Jon_Stewart)_ - _[Rolling Stone](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rolling_Stone)_ - _[Salon](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Salon_(website))_ - _[Sojourners](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sojourners)_ - _[Talking Points Memo](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Talking_Points_Memo)_ - _[ThinkProgress](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/ThinkProgress)_ - _[The Washington Post](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Washington_Post)_ - _[Vox (website)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vox_(website))_ |\n| See also - [Liberal bias in academia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Political_views_of_American_academics) - [Liberal bias in the media](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Media_bias_in_the_United_States) - _[The Liberal Imagination](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Liberal_Imagination)_(1950) - [Modern liberalism in the United States](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Modern_liberalism_in_the_United_States) - [American Left](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/American_Left) |\n| - [Liberalism portal](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Portal:Liberalism) - [United States portal](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Portal:United_States) |\n\nFor a chronological guide, see [Timeline of the Joe Biden presidency](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_the_Joe_Biden_presidency).\n\n### Inauguration\n\nMain article: [Inauguration of Joe Biden](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Inauguration_of_Joe_Biden)\n\nBiden takes [the oath of office](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Oath_of_office_of_the_President_of_the_United_States) administered by [Chief Justice](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chief_Justice_of_the_United_States) [John Roberts](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_Roberts) at [the Capitol](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_Capitol), January 20, 2021.\n\nBiden was inaugurated as the 46th president of the United States on January 20, 2021.[\\[336\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-hunnicutt-346)[\\[337\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-347) At 78, he was then the oldest person to assume the office up to that point.[\\[k\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-349)[\\[336\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-hunnicutt-346)[\\[339\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-350) Biden was the second [Catholic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Catholic) U.S. president, after [John F. Kennedy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_F._Kennedy),[\\[340\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-351)[\\[341\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-352) and the first president elected from the state of [Delaware](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Delaware).[\\[342\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-353) He was also the first person since [George H. W. Bush](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/George_H._W._Bush) to have been both vice president and president,[\\[343\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-354) and the only president to date from the [Silent Generation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Silent_Generation).[\\[344\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-355)[\\[345\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-356) Biden\'s inauguration was "a muted affair unlike any previous inauguration" due to COVID-19 precautions as well as massively increased security measures because of the [January 6 United States Capitol attack](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/January_6_United_States_Capitol_attack).[\\[346\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-357)\n\n### First 100 days\n\nMain article: [First 100 days of the Biden presidency](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/First_100_days_of_the_Biden_presidency)\n\nIn his first two days as president, Biden signed 17executive orders. By his third day, orders had included rejoining the [Paris Climate Agreement](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Paris_Climate_Agreement), ending the state of national emergency at the [border with Mexico](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mexico%E2%80%93United_States_border), directing the government to rejoin the [World Health Organization](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_Health_Organization), [face mask requirements](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/100_Days_Masking_Challenge) on [federal property](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Federal_lands), measures to combat [hunger in the United States](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hunger_in_the_United_States),[\\[l\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-362) and revoking permits for the construction of the [Keystone XL pipeline](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Keystone_XL_pipeline).[\\[351\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-363)[\\[352\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-364)[\\[353\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-365)\n\nBiden with [his Cabinet](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cabinet_of_Joe_Biden), July 2021\n\nOn March 11, Biden signed into law the [American Rescue Plan Act of 2021](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/American_Rescue_Plan_Act_of_2021), a $1.9 trillion [economic stimulus](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Stimulus_(economics)) and relief package that he had proposed to support the United States\' recovery from the [economic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Economic_impact_of_the_COVID-19_pandemic_in_the_United_States) and health effects of the [COVID-19 pandemic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/COVID-19_pandemic_in_the_United_States).[\\[354\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-366) The package included direct payments to most Americans, an extension of increased unemployment benefits, funds for vaccine distribution and school reopenings, and expansions of health insurance subsidies and the [child tax credit](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Child_tax_credit_(United_States)). Biden\'s initial proposal included an increase of the [federal minimum wage](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Minimum_wage_in_the_United_States) to $15 per hour, but after the [Senate parliamentarian](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Parliamentarian_of_the_United_States_Senate) determined that including the increase in a [budget reconciliation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Budget_reconciliation) bill would violate Senate rules, Democrats removed it.[\\[355\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-367)[\\[356\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-368)[\\[357\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-369)\n\nAlso in March, amid [a rise in migrants entering the U.S. from Mexico](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mexico%E2%80%93United_States_border_crisis), Biden said migrant adults were "being sent back", in reference to the continuation of the Trump administration\'s Title 42 policy for quick deportations.[\\[358\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-370) He earlier announced that his administration would not deport unaccompanied migrant children; the rise in arrivals of such children exceeded the capacity of facilities meant to shelter them, leading the Biden administration in March to direct the [Federal Emergency Management Agency](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Federal_Emergency_Management_Agency) to help.[\\[359\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-371)\n\nOn April 14, Biden announced that the United States [would delay the withdrawal of all troops](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2020%E2%80%932021_U.S._troop_withdrawal_from_Afghanistan) from the [war in Afghanistan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/War_in_Afghanistan_(2001%E2%80%932021)) until September 11, signaling an end to the country\'s direct military involvement in Afghanistan after nearly 20 years.[\\[360\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-372) In February 2020, the Trump administration had [made a deal](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States%E2%80%93Taliban_deal) with the Taliban to completely withdraw U.S. forces by May 1, 2021.[\\[361\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-images-373) Biden\'s decision met with a range of reactions, from support and relief to trepidation at the possible collapse of the Afghan government without American support.[\\[362\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-374) On April 22–23, Biden held an [international climate summit](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2021_Leaders%27_Climate_Summit) at which he announced that the U.S. would cut its [greenhouse gas emissions](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Greenhouse_gas_emissions) by 50%–52% by 2030 compared to 2005 levels.[\\[363\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-375)[\\[364\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-376) On April 28, the eve of his 100th day in office, Biden delivered his [first address to a joint session of Congress](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2021_Joe_Biden_speech_to_a_joint_session_of_Congress).[\\[365\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-377)\n\n### Domestic policy\n\nSee also: [Social policy of the Biden administration](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Social_policy_of_the_Biden_administration)\n\nBiden delivers a [speech at a joint session of Congress](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2021_Joe_Biden_speech_to_a_joint_session_of_Congress) with Vice President [Kamala Harris](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kamala_Harris) and [House Speaker](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Speaker_of_the_United_States_House_of_Representatives) [Nancy Pelosi](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nancy_Pelosi) on April 28, 2021.\n\nOn June 17, Biden signed the [Juneteenth National Independence Day Act](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Juneteenth_National_Independence_Day_Act), which officially declared [Juneteenth](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Juneteenth) a [federal holiday](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Federal_holidays_in_the_United_States).[\\[366\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-378) In July 2021, amid a slowing of [the COVID-19 vaccination rate in the country](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/COVID-19_vaccination_in_the_United_States) and the spread of the [SARS-CoV-2 Delta variant](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/SARS-CoV-2_Delta_variant), Biden said that it was "gigantically important" for Americans to be vaccinated.[\\[367\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-379)\n\nIn 2022, Biden endorsed a change to the [Senate filibuster](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Filibuster_in_the_United_States_Senate) to allow for the passing of the [Freedom to Vote Act](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Freedom_to_Vote_Act) and [John Lewis Voting Rights Act](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_Lewis_Voting_Rights_Act).[\\[368\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-380) The rules change failed when two Democratic senators joined Senate Republicans in opposing it.[\\[369\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-381) In April 2022, Biden signed into law the bipartisan [Postal Service Reform Act of 2022](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Postal_Service_Reform_Act_of_2022) to revamp the finances and operations of the [United States Postal Service](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_Postal_Service) agency.[\\[370\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-382) Biden supported the [Bipartisan Safer Communities Act](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bipartisan_Safer_Communities_Act) aimed to address gun reform issues following the [Robb Elementary School shooting](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Robb_Elementary_School_shooting) in [Uvalde, Texas](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Uvalde,_Texas);[\\[371\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-383) he signed the bill on June 25, 2022.[\\[372\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-384)\n\nThe [Honoring our PACT Act of 2022](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Honoring_our_PACT_Act_of_2022) was introduced in 2021 and signed into law by Biden on August 10, 2022.[\\[373\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-385) The act intended to significantly improve healthcare access and funding for veterans who were exposed to toxic substances, including [burn pits](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Burn_pits), during military service.[\\[374\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-386)\n\nIn 2022, Biden signed the [Respect for Marriage Act](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Respect_for_Marriage_Act), which repealed the [Defense of Marriage Act](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Defense_of_Marriage_Act) and requires the federal government to recognize the validity of [same-sex](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Same-sex_marriage_in_the_United_States) and [interracial](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Interracial_marriage_in_the_United_States) marriages.[\\[375\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-387)\n\nIn June 2024, Biden issued an executive action offering amnesty to unauthorized immigrants married to American citizens. The program included a pathway to U.S. residency and citizenship and was expected to initially affect about 500,000 people. It was later struck down due to a lack of legislation empowering the president to enact the program.[\\[376\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-388)[\\[377\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-389)\n\nIn January 2025, Biden declared the lapsed [Equal Rights Amendment](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Equal_Rights_Amendment) ratified as the "28th Amendment" to the [constitution](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Constitution_of_the_United_States). The declaration has no formal effect[\\[378\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-Stokols-390)[\\[379\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-391) and the [National Archives](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/National_Archives_of_the_United_States) has said it does not intend to certify the amendment as part of the constitution due to "established legal, judicial, and procedural decisions".[\\[380\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-392)\n\n#### Economic policy\n\nMain article: [Economic policy of the Biden administration](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Economic_policy_of_the_Biden_administration)\n\nInflation rate, United States and eurozone, January 2018 through November 2024\n\nBiden entered office nine months into a recovery from the [COVID-19 recession](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/COVID-19_recession) and his first year in office was characterized by robust growth in real GDP, employment, wages, and stock market returns, amid [significantly elevated inflation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2021%E2%80%932022_inflation_surge). Real GDP grew 5.9%, the fastest rate in 37 years.[\\[381\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-393)[\\[382\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-394) Amid record job creation, the unemployment rate fell at the fastest pace on record.[\\[383\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-395)[\\[384\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-396)[\\[385\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-397) By the end of 2021, inflation rates measured by the consumer price index (CPI) reached a nearly 40-year high of 7.1%, which was partially offset by the highest nominal wage and salary growth in at least 20 years. The inflation rate peaked at 9% in June 2022.[\\[m\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-403) The inflation rate reached 2.9% and core inflation rate reached 3.2% on an annual basis in December 2024, the last full month of Biden\'s term. Between December 2020 and December 2024, CPI rose 21.3% overall, with an annualized inflation rate of 5.3% throughout Biden\'s term in office. The inflation rate remained above the Federal Reserve\'s 2% target every month since March 2021, resulting in elevated interest rates to combat inflation. Average wages increased 19% throughout Biden\'s presidency, falling behind inflation. The unemployment rate declined by over 2% and real GDP grew 11% during Biden\'s term. Total household net worth increased by 28%, largely driven by stocks and real estate. The national debt grew to $36.2 trillion, with a debt to GDP ratio of 123% and a deficit to GDP ratio of 6% in FY 2024.[\\[391\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-404)[\\[386\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-chartingecon-398)[\\[392\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-405) In February 2023, the unemployment rate fell to 3.4%, a 53-year low.[\\[393\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-406)\n\nPercentage of uninsured Americans under age 65 from 2010 to 2022. The number and percentage of those uninsured under Biden fell to their lowest levels since 1997.[\\[394\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-NCHS_H122-407)\n\nAmid a surge in [inflation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2021%E2%80%932023_inflation_surge) and [high gas prices](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2021%E2%80%93present_global_energy_crisis), Biden\'s approval ratings declined, with his disapproval rating surpassing his approval rating in early 2022.[\\[395\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-408)[\\[396\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-409)[\\[397\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-410) After 5.9% growth in 2021, real GDP growth cooled in 2022 to 2.1%, after slightly negative growth in the first half spurred recession concerns. Job creation and consumer spending remained strong, as the unemployment rate fell to match a 53-year low of 3.5% in December. Inflation peaked at 9.1% in June before easing to 3.2% by October 2023. Stocks had had their worst year since 2008[\\[398\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-411)[\\[399\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-412)[\\[400\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-413) before recovering. Widespread predictions of an imminent recession did not materialize in 2022 or 2023, and by late 2023 indicators showed sharply lower inflation with economic acceleration. GDP growth hit 4.9% in the third quarter of 2023 and the year ended with stocks near record highs, with robust holiday spending.[\\[401\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-414)[\\[402\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-415)[\\[403\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-416)\n\nBiden signed numerous major pieces of economic legislation in the [117th Congress](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/117th_United_States_Congress), including the [American Rescue Plan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/American_Rescue_Plan_Act_of_2021), [Infrastructure Investment and Jobs Act](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Infrastructure_Investment_and_Jobs_Act), [CHIPS and Science Act](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/CHIPS_and_Science_Act), and the [Inflation Reduction Act](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Inflation_Reduction_Act).[\\[404\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-417) He signed the CHIPS and Science Act into law on August 9, 2022.[\\[405\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-418) It provided billions of dollars in new funding to boost domestic research on and manufacture of [semiconductors](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Semiconductors), to [compete economically with China](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/China%E2%80%93United_States_relations#Economic_relations).[\\[406\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-419) In his third month in office, Biden also signed an executive order to increase the minimum wage for federal contractors to $15 per hour. The order went into effect for 390,000 workers in January 2022.[\\[407\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-420)[\\[408\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-421) His administration rigorously enforced [antitrust law](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_antitrust_law).\n\nIn 2022, Biden blocked a [national railroad strike](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_United_States_railroad_labor_dispute) planned by multiple labor unions.[\\[409\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-422) During the [United Auto Workers strike](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2023_United_Auto_Workers_strike), he expressed support for the workers.[\\[410\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-423) Biden joined striking UAW workers\' [picket line](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Picketing) in Michigan, becoming the first president to join a picket line.[\\[411\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-424) He refused to block a [port strike](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2024_United_States_port_strike) from the [International Longshoremen\'s Association](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/International_Longshoremen%27s_Association) in October 2024.[\\[412\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-425)\n\nOver the course of five days in March 2023, [three small- to mid-size U.S. banks failed](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2023_banking_crisis), triggering a sharp decline in global bank stock prices and swift response by regulators to prevent potential global [contagion](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Financial_contagion). After [Silicon Valley Bank collapsed](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Collapse_of_Silicon_Valley_Bank), the first to do so, Biden expressed opposition to a bailout by taxpayers.[\\[413\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-426) He claimed that the [partial rollback](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Economic_Growth,_Regulatory_Relief,_and_Consumer_Protection_Act) of [Dodd-Frank regulations](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dodd%E2%80%93Frank_Wall_Street_Reform_and_Consumer_Protection_Act) contributed to the bank\'s failure.[\\[414\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-427)\n\nAt the beginning of the [118th Congress](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/118th_United_States_Congress), Biden and congressional Republicans [engaged in a standoff](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2023_United_States_debt-ceiling_crisis) after the U.S. hit its [debt limit](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_debt_ceiling), which raised the risk that the U.S. would [default](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Default_(finance)) on its debt.[\\[415\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-428) Biden and House speaker [Kevin McCarthy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kevin_McCarthy) struck a deal to raise the debt limit, the [Fiscal Responsibility Act of 2023](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fiscal_Responsibility_Act_of_2023), which suspended the debt limit until January 2025. Biden signed it on June 3, averting a default.[\\[416\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-429) The deal was generally seen as favorable to Biden.[\\[417\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-430)[\\[418\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-431)\n\nBiden extended the COVID-19 student loan pause through September 2023, with an "on ramp" period that extended some of the pause\'s protections against credit reporting, collection efforts, and late payment fees through September 30, 2024.[\\[419\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-432) The Biden administration\'s attempts to implement student loan forgiveness and relief programs have faced legal challenges from a coalition of Republican-led states.[\\[420\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-433) Biden\'s plans to forgive student loan debt were estimated to cost over $519 billion,[\\[421\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-434) and some critics called them a "disaster".[\\[422\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-435)\n\n#### Judiciary\n\nFurther information: [List of federal judges appointed by Joe Biden](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_federal_judges_appointed_by_Joe_Biden)\n\nBiden and [Ketanji Brown Jackson](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ketanji_Brown_Jackson) watching the [U.S. Senate](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_Senate) vote on her confirmation, April 2022\n\nBy the end of 2021, 40 of his nominees to the federal judiciary had been confirmed, more than any president in his first year in office since [Ronald Reagan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ronald_Reagan).[\\[423\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-436) Biden prioritized diversity in his judicial appointments more than any president in U.S. history, with most of his appointees being women and people of color.[\\[424\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-437)\n\nIn January 2022, Supreme Court justice [Stephen Breyer](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Stephen_Breyer) announced his intention to retire. During his 2020 campaign, Biden vowed to nominate the first Black woman to the Supreme Court if a vacancy occurred,[\\[425\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-438) a promise he reiterated after Breyer announced his retirement.[\\[426\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-439) On February 25, [Biden nominated](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ketanji_Brown_Jackson_Supreme_Court_nomination) federal judge [Ketanji Brown Jackson](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ketanji_Brown_Jackson).[\\[427\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-440) She was sworn in on June 30.[\\[428\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-441) By the end of his presidency, Biden had appointed 235 judges, more appointments in a single term than any other president in at least 50 years. 63% of Biden\'s judges were women and 60% were non-white.[\\[429\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-442)[\\[430\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-443) Biden expressed interest in judicial [term limits](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Term_limits_in_the_United_States#Federal_term_limits) and a binding ethics code for Supreme Court justices.[\\[431\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-BidenSCOTUSreform-444)\n\n#### Infrastructure and climate\n\nFurther information: [Build Back Better Plan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Build_Back_Better_Plan) and [Environmental policy of the Biden administration](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Environmental_policy_of_the_Biden_administration)\n\nBiden, then British prime minister [Boris Johnson](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boris_Johnson) and UN secretary-general [António Guterres](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ant%C3%B3nio_Guterres) at the opening ceremony of the [COP26 climate summit](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_Nations_Climate_Change_conference) in Glasgow on November 1, 2021\n\nAs part of Biden\'s Build Back Better agenda, in late March 2021, he proposed the [American Jobs Plan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/American_Jobs_Plan), a $2 trillion package addressing issues including transport infrastructure, utilities infrastructure, broadband infrastructure, housing, schools, manufacturing, research and workforce development.[\\[432\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-445)[\\[433\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-446) After months of negotiations among Biden and lawmakers, in August 2021 the Senate passed a $1 trillion bipartisan infrastructure bill called the [Infrastructure Investment and Jobs Act](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Infrastructure_Investment_and_Jobs_Act),[\\[434\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-447)[\\[435\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-448) while the House, also in a bipartisan manner, approved that bill in early November 2021, covering infrastructure related to transport, utilities, and broadband.[\\[436\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-449) Biden signed the bill into law in mid-November 2021.[\\[437\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-450)\n\nThe other core part of the Build Back Better agenda was the [Build Back Better Act](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Build_Back_Better_Act), a $3.5 trillion social spending bill that expands the [social safety net](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Social_safety_net) and includes major provisions on climate change.[\\[438\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-451)[\\[439\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-452) Democrats attempted to pass it on a [party-line vote](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Party-line_vote) through [budget reconciliation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Reconciliation_(United_States_Congress)), but struggled to win the support of Senator [Joe Manchin](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Joe_Manchin), even as the price was lowered to $2.2 trillion.[\\[440\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-453) After Manchin rejected the bill,[\\[441\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-454) it was comprehensively reworked into the [Inflation Reduction Act of 2022](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Inflation_Reduction_Act_of_2022), covering deficit reduction, climate change, healthcare, and tax reform.[\\[442\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-455)\n\nThe [Inflation Reduction Act of 2022](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Inflation_Reduction_Act_of_2022) was introduced by Manchin and Senator [Chuck Schumer](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chuck_Schumer).[\\[443\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-456)[\\[444\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-457) The package aimed to raise $739 billion and authorize $370 billion in spending on energy and [climate change](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change), $300 billion in deficit reduction, three years of [Affordable Care Act](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Affordable_Care_Act) subsidies, prescription drug reform to lower prices, and [tax reform](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tax_reform).[\\[445\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-458) According to an analysis by the Rhodium Group, the bill will lower [U.S. greenhouse gas emissions](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change_in_the_United_States) between 31 percent and 44 percent below 2005 levels by 2030.[\\[446\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-Joan-459) On August 7, 2022, the Senate passed the bill (as amended) on a 51–50 vote, with all Democrats voting in favor, all Republicans opposed, and Vice President [Kamala Harris](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kamala_Harris) [breaking the tie](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_tie-breaking_votes_cast_by_the_vice_president_of_the_United_States). Biden signed the bill on August 16.[\\[447\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-460)[\\[448\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-461)\n\nBefore and during the [2021 United Nations Climate Change Conference](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2021_United_Nations_Climate_Change_Conference) (COP26), Biden promoted an agreement that the U.S. and the [European Union](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/European_Union) cut methane emissions by a third by 2030 and tried to add dozens of other countries to the effort.[\\[449\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-462) Biden pledged to double climate funding to developing countries by 2024.[\\[450\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-463) Also at COP26, the U.S. and China reached a deal on greenhouse gas emission reduction. The two countries are responsible for 40 percent of global emissions.[\\[451\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-464) In July 2023, when [heat waves hit the United States](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2023_Western_North_America_heat_wave), Biden announced measures to protect the population and said the heat waves were linked to climate change.[\\[452\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-465)[\\[453\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-466) In April 2024, he unveiled a plan to protect and restore natural water sources (3.2 million hectares of [wetlands](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wetland) and 161,000\xa0km of waterways).[\\[454\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-467)\n\nBiden protected 674 million acres of land and ocean from natural resource exploitation, more than any other president. The vast majority of the conservation came from a ban on offshore drilling in 625 million acres of ocean.[\\[455\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-468)[\\[456\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-469)\n\n#### Immigration\n\nMain article: [Immigration policy of the Biden administration](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Immigration_policy_of_the_Biden_administration)\n\nYearly numbers of illegal immigrants apprehended at the [U.S. southern border](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mexico%E2%80%93United_States_border)\n\nIllegal border crossings at the [Mexico–United States border](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mexico%E2%80%93United_States_border) began to surge in 2021 when Biden assumed office,[\\[n\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-474) reaching an all-time monthly high in December 2023.[\\[461\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-475)[\\[462\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-476) Throughout 2024, crossings began to significantly decline from the December record, after Biden implemented restrictions on [asylum](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Asylum_in_the_United_States) claims from migrants who cross the border between ports of entry and urged Mexico to crack down on migrants.[\\[463\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-cbs-border-crossings-477)[\\[464\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-478)[\\[465\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-479) Deportations from October 2023 to September 2024 reached the highest level since 2014.[\\[466\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-480) Biden used [humanitarian parole](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Humanitarian_parole) to mitigate illegal border crossings, allowing migrants to fly into the U.S. or schedule their entries through official entry points in the U.S.-Mexico border. Over a million migrants had been admitted to the U.S. under humanitarian parole as of January 2024.[\\[467\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-481)[\\[468\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-482)[\\[469\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-483)\n\nBiden visiting border patrol agents at the U.S. southern border, January 2023\n\nIn January 2024, Biden expressed support for a proposed bipartisan immigration deal led by Senators [Kyrsten Sinema](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kyrsten_Sinema) and [James Lankford](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/James_Lankford). He had previously supported the [U.S. Citizenship Act of 2021](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/U.S._Citizenship_Act_of_2021), which he proposed on his first day in office.[\\[470\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-484)[\\[471\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-485) The proposed bipartisan bill would have allowed [DHS](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Department_of_Homeland_Security) to close the border when encounters reach a seven-day average of 5,000 or exceed 8,500 in a single day.[\\[472\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-486)[\\[473\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-487) In addition, the bill would have mandated the detention of migrants seeking asylum and undergoing asylum interviews, with those failing the process repatriated to their home countries.[\\[474\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-488) While not addressing the status of " [Dreamers](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Deferred_Action_for_Childhood_Arrivals)", it would have changed immigration law to allow the children of those with [H-1B visas](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/H-1B_visas) to get work authorizations and freeze their legal ages while waiting for green cards, rather than face deportation once they turn 21, and provide additional funding for immigration judges.[\\[475\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-489)\n\nFormer president Donald Trump announced his opposition to the legislation, calling on Congressional Republicans to oppose it; subsequently, leaders such as [Speaker of the House](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Speaker_of_the_United_States_House_of_Representatives) [Mike Johnson](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mike_Johnson) announced their opposition, halting further legislative action.[\\[476\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-490)[\\[477\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-491) As a result of continued high immigration levels throughout his tenure, some lawmakers and pundits have criticized Biden\'s handling of the southern border.[\\[478\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-492)[\\[479\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-493)[\\[480\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-494) Criticism of the bill and broader immigration policy continued to be expressed by both sides, with some liberals considering his policies too harsh while some conservatives considered them too lax.[\\[481\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-495)[\\[482\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-496) On January 17, 2024, a Republican-led non-binding resolution denouncing the Biden-Harris administration\'s handling of the U.S. southern border passed the House of Representatives by a vote of 225–187, with 211 Republicans and 14 Democrats supporting it.[\\[483\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-497) In the final year of his presidency, the Biden administration worked to extend at least 14 contracts with private prison companies to run immigrant detention centers, despite his 2020 campaign promise to end the practice.[\\[484\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-498) In June 2024, Biden issued an [executive order](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/A_Proclamation_on_Securing_the_Border) allowing the president to restrict the Mexico–U.S. border.[\\[485\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-499)[\\[463\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-cbs-border-crossings-477)\n\n#### Pardons and commutations\n\nBiden issued more individual pardons and commutations than any other president.[\\[486\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-APpardons-500) On October 6, 2022, he pardoned all Americans convicted of "small" amounts of [cannabis](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cannabis_(drug)) possession under federal law.[\\[487\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-501) On December 22, 2023, he pardoned Americans for cannabis use or possession on federal lands regardless of whether they had been charged or prosecuted.[\\[488\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-502)[\\[489\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-503) On December 12, 2024, in the largest single-day clemency act in history, Biden granted clemency to about 1,500 nonviolent felons in [home confinement](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Home_confinement) who had previously been released from prison.[\\[490\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-504)[\\[491\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-505) The act generated controversy, as it included felons such as [Michael Conahan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Michael_Conahan), a judge involved in the [kids for cash kickback scandal](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kids_for_cash), and [Rita Crundwell](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rita_Crundwell), a comptroller responsible for the single largest municipal fraud in U.S. history. The Biden administration said the offenders who received clemency "deserve a second chance" and were selected based on meeting certain criteria in a uniform decision.[\\[492\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-506)[\\[493\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-507) On December 23, 2024, Biden commuted the sentences of 37 out of 40 federal [death row](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Death_row) inmates.[\\[494\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-508) On his last day in office, Biden commuted the sentence of [Leonard Peltier](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leonard_Peltier), convicted of murdering two FBI agents, to house arrest.[\\[495\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-509)\n\n#### Pardons of family members and political figures\n\nPardon dated December 1, 2024\n\nBiden issued more pardons for members of his family than any other president.[\\[496\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-lastpardonnyt-510) On December 1, 2024, he issued a "full and unconditional" pardon to Hunter Biden that covered all federal offenses between 2014 and December 1, 2024. The pardon\'s sweeping extent was "unprecedented".[\\[497\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-:2-511) According to [_Reason_](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Reason_(magazine)) magazine, Hunter Biden\'s pardon was even more far-reaching than [Richard Nixon](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Richard_Nixon)\'s or other "controversial"[\\[497\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-:2-511) pardons:\n\n> The Hunter pardon is far more comprehensive...in that it covered not just his convictions for drug-related activities and tax fraud, but _any other criminal behavior_ since 2014—the year that Hunter joined the board of Ukrainian energy company Burisma. It has been alleged that Hunter\'s job was essentially to trade on the family name and sell his access to dad. This may not have been illegal, but it does mean that the pardon is clearly designed to offer preemptive protection not just to Hunter, but to Joe Biden himself. These features make the pardon unprecedented, though perfectly in line with the president\'s executive powers.\n\nHunter had been convicted on charges related to tax and gun offenses, after which Joe made numerous promises not to pardon him. He and his staff continued to say that Hunter would not be pardoned as late as November, although internal staff discussions affirmed that the option remained on the table even as Biden said otherwise.[\\[498\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-512)[\\[499\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-513)[\\[59\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-NBCpardon-61) Biden and his family finalized the decision to pardon Hunter without consulting senior staff.[\\[500\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-nytdec2-514) In a statement announcing the pardon, Biden said he believed his son was "selectively, and unfairly, prosecuted", blaming "political pressure" for the collapse of a plea bargain. The plea bargain actually fell apart after the presiding judge asked about its unusual construction.[\\[62\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-White_House_2024-64)[\\[501\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-515)[\\[502\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-516) Biden\'s pardon came amid incoming December sentencing dates for Hunter for his convictions and concerns about the succeeding Trump administration potentially targeting political rivals for prosecution.[\\[500\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-nytdec2-514) Biden said, "I hope Americans will understand why a father and a president would come to this decision."[\\[503\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-:1-517)\n\nOn his last day in office, Biden issued pardons for more of his family members and other high-profile figures.[\\[496\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-lastpardonnyt-510) The pardons covered Biden\'s siblings and their spouses, including [James Biden](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/James_Biden), who was interviewed as part of an impeachment probe into Biden. Others pardoned that day include former [chairman of the Joint Chiefs of Staff](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chairman_of_the_Joint_Chiefs_of_Staff) [Mark Milley](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mark_Milley), former [National Institute of Allergy and Infectious Diseases](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/National_Institute_of_Allergy_and_Infectious_Diseases) director [Anthony Fauci](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Anthony_Fauci), and members and participants in the [House Select Committee on the January 6 Attack](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/House_Select_Committee_on_the_January_6_Attack), despite many of those pardoned not having been under criminal investigation.[\\[496\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-lastpardonnyt-510)[\\[486\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-APpardons-500) Biden justified the pardons by citing his concern about "baseless and politically motivated investigations" during Trump\'s second term.[\\[504\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-518)[\\[505\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-519)[\\[506\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-520) Biden added that the pardons were preemptive and should not be seen as implying their recipients\' guilt.[\\[507\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-521)[\\[508\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-522) The pardons Biden granted to his family and other political figures had a sweeping scope similar to the one he granted Hunter, covering federal offenses the recipients committed or may have committed between 2014 and the day of the pardon.[\\[486\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-APpardons-500)[\\[509\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-523)\n\nBiden also pardoned two other Democratic officials on his last day in office: Ernest William Cromartie, convicted of [tax evasion](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tax_evasion), and [Gerald G. Lundergan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gerald_G._Lundergan), convicted of a scheme to funnel money to his daughter\'s Senate campaign.[\\[510\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-524)[\\[511\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-525)[\\[512\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-526)\n\n#### 2022 elections\n\nMain article: [2022 United States elections](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_United_States_elections)\n\nBiden holding a rally at [Bowie State University](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bowie_State_University) in [Maryland](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Maryland) for gubernatorial candidate [Wes Moore](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wes_Moore), November 7, 2022\n\nOn September 2, 2022, in a nationally broadcast [Philadelphia speech](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Battle_for_the_Soul_of_the_Nation_speech), Biden called for a "battle for the soul of the nation". Off camera, he called Trump supporters "semi-fascists", which Republican commentators denounced.[\\[513\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-527)[\\[514\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-528)[\\[515\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-529) A predicted Republican [wave election](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wave_elections_in_the_United_States) did not materialize and the race for [U.S. Congress](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/U.S._Congress) control was much closer than expected, with Republicans securing a slim majority of [222seats in the House of Representatives](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_United_States_House_of_Representatives_elections),[\\[o\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-534) and the Democratic caucus keeping control of the [U.S. Senate](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_United_States_Senate_elections).[\\[520\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-535)[\\[p\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-539)\n\nIt was the first midterm election since [1986](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1986_United_States_gubernatorial_elections) in which the incumbent president\'s party achieved a net gain in governorships, and the first since [1934](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1934_United_States_elections) in which the president\'s party lost no state legislative chambers.[\\[524\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-540) Democrats credited Biden for their unexpectedly strong performance,[\\[525\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-541) but they likely overperformed for other reasons, including [the Supreme Court overturning _Roe v. Wade_](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dobbs_v._Jackson_Women%27s_Health_Organization) and poor Republican candidate quality in many races.[\\[526\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-542)[\\[527\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-543)\n\n### Foreign policy\n\nMain article: [Foreign policy of the Biden administration](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Foreign_policy_of_the_Biden_administration)\n\nIn June 2021, Biden took his first trip abroad as president, visiting Belgium, Switzerland, and the United Kingdom. He attended [a G7 summit](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/47th_G7_summit), [a NATO summit](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2021_Brussels_NATO_summit), and an EU summit, and held [one-on-one talks](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2021_Russia%E2%80%93United_States_summit) with Russian president [Vladimir Putin](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Putin).[\\[528\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-544)\n\nIn September 2021, Biden announced [AUKUS](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/AUKUS), a [security pact](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Defense_pact) between Australia, the United Kingdom and the United States, to ensure "peace and stability
