in the [Indo-Pacific](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Indo-Pacific)".[\\[529\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-545)\n\nIn February 2021, the Biden administration announced that the United States was ending its [support for the Saudi-led bombing campaign](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/U.S._support_for_Saudi-led_operations_in_Yemen) in Yemen and revoked the designation of Yemen\'s [Houthis](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Houthis) as terrorists.[\\[530\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-546)[\\[531\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-547) In early February 2022, Biden ordered the counterterrorism raid in northern Syria that resulted in the [death of Abu Ibrahim al-Hashimi al-Qurashi](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Abu_Ibrahim_al-Hashimi_al-Qurashi#Death), the second leader of the [Islamic State](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Islamic_State).[\\[532\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-548) In late July, Biden approved the [drone strike](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Drone_strike) that [killed Ayman al-Zawahiri](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Killing_of_Ayman_al-Zawahiri), the second leader of [Al-Qaeda](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Al-Qaeda), and an integral member in the planning of the [September 11 attacks](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/September_11_attacks).[\\[533\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-549) The [2022 OPEC+ oil production cut](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/OPEC#2022_oil_production_cut) caused a diplomatic spat with Saudi Arabia, threatening a longstanding [alliance](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Saudi_Arabia%E2%80%93United_States_relations).[\\[534\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-550)[\\[535\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-551)\n\nIn August 2024, Biden negotiated and oversaw the [2024 Ankara prisoner exchange](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2024_Ankara_prisoner_exchange), the largest [prisoner exchange](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Prisoner_exchange) since the end of the [Cold War](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War). It involved the release of 26 people, including journalist [Evan Gershkovich](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Evan_Gershkovich) and former Marine [Paul Whelan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Paul_Whelan).[\\[536\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-552) In November 2024, the Biden administration announced that it had helped broker a [ceasefire](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2024_Israel%E2%80%93Lebanon_ceasefire_agreement) agreement in the [Israel–Hezbollah conflict](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel%E2%80%93Hezbollah_conflict_(2023%E2%80%932024)).[\\[q\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-557)\n\n#### Withdrawal from Afghanistan\n\nMain article: [2020–2021 U.S. troop withdrawal from Afghanistan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2020%E2%80%932021_U.S._troop_withdrawal_from_Afghanistan)\n\nBiden in a video conference with Vice President [Kamala Harris](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kamala_Harris) and the [U.S. National Security team](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_National_Security_Council), discussing the [Fall of Kabul](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fall_of_Kabul_(2021)) on August 15, 2021\n\nAmerican forces had begun withdrawing from Afghanistan in 2020, under the provisions of a [February 2020 US-Taliban agreement](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States%E2%80%93Taliban_deal) that set a May 1, 2021, deadline.[\\[541\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-558) The Taliban began [an offensive](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2021_Taliban_offensive) on May 1.[\\[542\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-559)[\\[543\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-560) By early July, most American troops in Afghanistan had withdrawn.[\\[361\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-images-373) Biden addressed the withdrawal in July, saying, "The likelihood there\'s going to be the Taliban overrunning everything and owning the whole country is highly unlikely."[\\[361\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-images-373)\n\nOn August 15, [the Afghan government collapsed](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fall_of_Kabul_(2021)) under the Taliban offensive, and Afghan President [Ashraf Ghani](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ashraf_Ghani) fled the country.[\\[361\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-images-373)[\\[544\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-messy-561) Biden reacted by ordering 6,000 American troops to assist with evacuating American personnel and Afghan allies.[\\[545\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-562) He faced bipartisan criticism for the manner of the withdrawal,[\\[546\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-563) with the evacuations described as chaotic and botched.[\\[547\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-564)[\\[548\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-565)[\\[549\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-566) On August 16, Biden addressed the "messy" situation, taking responsibility for it, and admitting that the situation "unfolded more quickly than we had anticipated".[\\[544\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-messy-561)[\\[550\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-buck1-567) He defended his decision to withdraw, saying that Americans should not be "dying in a war that Afghan forces are not willing to fight for themselves".[\\[550\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-buck1-567)[\\[551\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-568)\n\nOn August 26, a [suicide bombing at the Kabul airport](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2021_Kabul_airport_attack) killed 13 U.S. service members and 169 Afghans. On August 27, an American drone strike killed two ISIS-K targets, who were "planners and facilitators", according to a U.S. Army general.[\\[552\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-569) The U.S. military completed its withdrawal from Afghanistan on August 30. Biden called the extraction of over 120,000 Americans, Afghans, and other allies "an extraordinary success".[\\[553\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-570) He acknowledged that up to 200 Americans who wanted to leave did not, despite his August 18 pledge to keep troops in Afghanistan until all Americans who wanted to leave had left.[\\[554\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-571)\n\nAfter the withdrawal, the U.S. continued to send aid to Afghanistan, remaining its biggest aid donor as of August 2024 and spending at least $20.7 billion post-withdrawal. U.S. funding has helped support the Taliban government and stabilize Afghanistan\'s economy.[\\[555\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-572)[\\[556\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-573) On September 25, 2024, the [United States House of Representatives](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_House_of_Representatives) passed a resolution condemning the Biden administration for the U.S. withdrawal from Afghanistan, with ten Democrats and all Republicans voting in favor.[\\[557\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-574)\n\n#### Russian invasion of Ukraine\n\nFurther information: [Russian invasion of Ukraine](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Russian_invasion_of_Ukraine) and [United States and the Russian invasion of Ukraine](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_and_the_Russian_invasion_of_Ukraine)\n\nBiden with [refugees from Ukraine](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ukrainian_refugee_crisis) in [Warsaw](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Warsaw), Poland, March 2022\n\nIn February 2022, the [Russian Armed Forces](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Russian_Armed_Forces) under President [Vladimir Putin](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Putin) launched [an invasion of Ukraine](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Russian_invasion_of_Ukraine). After warning for several weeks that an attack was imminent, Biden responded by imposing severe [sanctions on Russia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/International_sanctions_during_the_2022_Russian_invasion_of_Ukraine) and authorizing over $8 billion in [weapons shipments to Ukraine](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_military_aid_to_Ukraine_during_the_Russo-Ukrainian_War).[\\[558\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-575)[\\[559\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-576)[\\[560\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-577) On April 29, he asked Congress for $33 billion for Ukraine,[\\[561\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-578)[\\[562\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-579) but lawmakers later increased it to about $40 billion.[\\[563\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-580)[\\[564\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-581)[\\[565\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-582) Biden blamed Putin for the emerging [energy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2021%E2%80%93present_global_energy_crisis) and [food crises](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_food_crises).[\\[566\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-583)[\\[567\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-584)[\\[568\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-585)\n\nIn 2022, Congress approved about $113 billion in aid to Ukraine.[\\[569\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-586) In October 2023, the Biden administration requested an additional $61.4 billion in aid for Ukraine for the year ahead,[\\[570\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-587) but delays in the passage of further aid by the [House of Representatives](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_House_of_Representatives) inhibited progress, with the additional $61\xa0billion in aid to Ukraine added in April 2024.[\\[571\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-588)[\\[572\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-589)[\\[573\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-590) Actually delivered aid often differed from announced levels and was also often delayed. The [Government Accountability Office](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Government_Accountability_Office) and [Pentagon Inspector General](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Department_of_Defense_Office_of_Inspector_General) found that the Biden administration seemed unaware of the pace of weapons deliveries.[\\[574\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-591)\n\nThroughout the conflict, Biden consistently refused Ukrainian requests to allow them to utilize weapons against Russian military targets inside [Russia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Russia). An exception was granted in May 2024 for targets in the vicinity of [Kharkiv](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kharkiv) for "counter-fire" purposes.[\\[r\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-596) Biden also blocked access for some weapons systems altogether, typically citing fears of escalation, only to permit deliveries for some weapons later on.[\\[s\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-602)\n\n#### China affairs\n\nFurther information: [China–United States relations §\xa0Biden administration (2021–2025)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/China%E2%80%93United_States_relations#Biden_administration_(2021%E2%80%932025))\n\nBiden with Chinese leader [Xi Jinping](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Xi_Jinping) during the [G20 summit in Bali](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_G20_Bali_summit), November 14, 2022Biden with Chinese leader [Xi Jinping](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Xi_Jinping) during the [APEC summit in Lima](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/APEC_Peru_2024), November 16, 2024\n\nThe [Solomon Islands-China security pact](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/China%E2%80%93Solomon_Islands_relations) caused alarm in late 2022, as China could build military bases across the South Pacific. Biden sought to strengthen ties with Australia and New Zealand in the wake of the deal.[\\[584\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-603)[\\[585\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-604)[\\[586\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-605) In a September 2022 interview with _[60 Minutes](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/60_Minutes)_, Biden said that U.S. forces would defend Taiwan in the event of "an unprecedented attack" by the Chinese,[\\[587\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-606) which is in contrast to the long-standing U.S. policy of " [strategic ambiguity](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Strategic_ambiguity)" toward China and Taiwan.[\\[588\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-Kine-607)[\\[589\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-608)[\\[590\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-609) The September comments came after three previous comments by Biden that the U.S. would defend Taiwan in the event of a Chinese invasion.[\\[591\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-theories-610) Amid increasing tension with China, Biden\'s administration has repeatedly walked back his statements and asserted that U.S. policy toward Taiwan has not changed.[\\[591\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-theories-610)[\\[592\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-611)[\\[588\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-Kine-607) In late 2022, Biden issued several executive orders and federal rules designed to slow Chinese technological growth, and maintain U.S. leadership over computing, biotech, and clean energy.[\\[593\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-612)\n\nOn February 4, 2023, Biden ordered the United States Air Force to shoot down a [suspected Chinese surveillance balloon](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2023_Chinese_balloon_incident) off the coast of [South Carolina](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Carolina).[\\[594\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-613)[\\[595\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-614) The [Chinese government](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chinese_government) denied that the balloon was a surveillance device, instead claiming it was a civilian [airship](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Airship) that had blown off course.[\\[596\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-615)[\\[597\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-616) Secretary of State [Antony Blinken](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Antony_Blinken) postponed his planned visit to China as the incident further damaged U.S.-China relations.[\\[598\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-617)[\\[599\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-618)[\\[600\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-619) In May 2024, the Biden administration doubled [tariffs](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tariff) on [solar cells](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_cell) imported from China and more than tripled tariffs on [lithium-ion electric vehicle batteries](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lithium-ion_battery) imported from China.[\\[601\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-erwgs-620) It also raised tariffs on imports of Chinese steel, aluminum, and medical materials.[\\[601\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-erwgs-620)\n\nIn April 2024, Biden signed the [Protecting Americans from Foreign Adversary Controlled Applications Act](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protecting_Americans_from_Foreign_Adversary_Controlled_Applications_Act), which would ban [social networking services](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Social_networking_service) if they are determined by the president and relevant provisions to be a "foreign adversary controlled application". The act explicitly applies to [ByteDance Ltd.](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/ByteDance) and its subsidiaries, which are based in China. It ceases to be applicable if the application is [divested](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Divestment) and no longer considered to be controlled by a [foreign adversary of the United States](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_foreign_adversaries#Other_meanings). Biden had signed the [No TikTok on Government Devices Act](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/No_TikTok_on_Government_Devices_Act) in December 2022, prohibiting the use of TikTok on devices owned by the federal government.[\\[602\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-621)[\\[603\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-622)[\\[604\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-623)\n\n#### Gaza war\n\nFurther information: [United States support for Israel in the Gaza war](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_support_for_Israel_in_the_Gaza_war)\n\nBiden with Israeli president [Isaac Herzog](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Isaac_Herzog) and prime minister [Benjamin Netanyahu](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Benjamin_Netanyahu) in Tel Aviv, Israel, October 18, 2023\n\nIn October 2023, Hamas [launched a surprise attack on Israel](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/October_7_attacks) that [devolved into an intensified conflict](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gaza_war), jeopardizing the administration\'s push to normalize relations [between Israel and Saudi Arabia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel%E2%80%93Saudi_Arabia_relations).[\\[605\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-624) Biden stated [his unequivocal support for Israel](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_support_for_Israel_in_the_Gaza_war) and condemned the attack by Hamas, but discouraged Israel from initiating a ground invasion of Gaza.[\\[606\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-625)[\\[607\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-WarWoodward-626) Upon Israel\'s retaliation against Hamas, Biden deployed aircraft carriers in the region to deter others from joining the war,[\\[608\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-627) and called for an additional $14 billion in military aid to Israel.[\\[609\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-628) He later began pressuring Israel to address the growing [humanitarian crisis in the Gaza Strip](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2023_Israeli_blockade_of_the_Gaza_Strip).[\\[610\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-629) Biden rejected calls for a ceasefire but said he supported "humanitarian pauses" to deliver aid to the [Gaza Strip](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gaza_Strip).[\\[611\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-630) He asked Israel to pause its invasion of Gaza for at least three days to allow for hostage negotiations; Israel agreed to daily four-hour pauses.[\\[612\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-631) He also directed the U.S. military to facilitate the delivery of humanitarian aid to Palestinians in Gaza.[\\[613\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-632) Biden has said he is a [Zionist](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Zionist).[\\[614\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-633)[\\[615\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-634) He has faced criticism for his unwavering support for Israel. Officials have urged him to take a harder stance against Israel, criticizing his administration\'s leniency and support despite the Israeli government\'s contentious offensive, which has led to significant civilian casualties and [humanitarian crises](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gaza_humanitarian_crisis_(2023%E2%80%93present)).[\\[616\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-635)[\\[617\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-636)[\\[618\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-637)\n\nFollowing the [killing of Palestinian civilians receiving food aid](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Flour_massacre) on February 29, 2024, Biden said the current level of aid flowing into Gaza was insufficient.[\\[619\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-638) On March 3, the U.S. military began airdropping food aid into Gaza.[\\[620\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-639) Several experts called the U.S. airdrops performative and said they would do little to alleviate the [famine in Gaza](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gaza_Strip_famine).[\\[621\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-640)\n\nBiden continued to support Israel during the course of the war despite significant domestic opposition to American involvement in it and subsequent widespread [protests](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gaza_war_protests_in_the_United_States). A March 2024 Gallup poll found that a strong majority of Americans disapproved of Israeli conduct during the war.[\\[622\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-Gallup_Inc.-641) Beginning in April 2024, widespread [Gaza war protests emerged on university campuses](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_pro-Palestinian_protests_on_university_campuses_in_the_United_States_in_2024), denouncing Biden.[\\[623\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-642)\n\nOn May 31, 2024, Biden announced his support for an Israeli [ceasefire](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/January_2025_Gaza_war_ceasefire) proposal, saying that Hamas was "no longer capable" of another large-scale attack.[\\[624\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-643)[\\[625\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-644)[\\[626\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-645) The proposal, which was intended to establish a permanent ceasefire, bring about the release of all hostages, and lead to the reconstruction of the [Gaza Strip](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gaza_Strip), was supported by Hamas officials after mediation by [Egypt](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Egypt) and [Qatar](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Qatar).[\\[627\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-646)[\\[628\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-647) The Netanyahu administration responded that Israel\'s goals regarding "the destruction of Hamas military and governing capabilities" had not changed and that conditions would need to be met before it would agree to a ceasefire.[\\[629\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-648)[\\[630\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-649)[\\[631\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-650) In the first year of the war, it was estimated that the Biden administration had sent Israel at least $17.9 billion in military aid, a record.[\\[632\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-knickmeyer-651) In about the same period, it sent Palestinians $1.2 billion in humanitarian aid.[\\[633\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-ching-voa-652) Biden was reported by journalist [Bob Woodward](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bob_Woodward) to have clashed throughout the war with Netanyahu regarding his war strategy and lack of a post-war plan for Gaza.[\\[607\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-WarWoodward-626) In the last week of Biden\'s presidency, Qatari officials announced that Hamas had accepted the ceasefire deal; Biden hailed the deal.[\\[634\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-653)[\\[635\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-654)\n\n#### NATO enlargement\n\nFollowing the [2022 Russian invasion of Ukraine](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_Russian_invasion_of_Ukraine), Biden expressed support for expanding [NATO](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/NATO) to cover [Sweden](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sweden) and [Finland](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Finland).[\\[636\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-655)[\\[637\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-656) On August 9, 2022, he signed the instruments of ratification stipulating U.S. support for the two countries\' entry into NATO.[\\[638\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-657)[\\[639\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-658) [Finnish ascension](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Finland%E2%80%93NATO_relations) occurred on April 4, 2023, but opposition by [Turkey](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Turkey) and [Hungary](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hungary) to [Swedish entry](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sweden%E2%80%93NATO_relations) led to a stalemate.[\\[640\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-659) Biden led diplomatic talks resulting in formal Swedish ascension into NATO on March 7, 2024.[\\[641\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-660)[\\[642\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-661) He has also expressed openness to [Ukrainian](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ukraine) entry into NATO following the end of the conflict,[\\[643\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-662) supporting an expedited timetable in its ascension and the removal of steps such as the [Membership Action Plan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Enlargement_of_NATO#Membership_Action_Plan) typically required for NATO entry.[\\[644\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-663)[\\[645\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-664)\n\n### Investigations\n\n#### Retention of classified documents\n\nMain article: [Joe Biden classified documents incident](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Joe_Biden_classified_documents_incident)\n\nIn November 2022, Biden\'s attorneys found classified documents dating from his vice presidency in a "locked closet" at the [Penn Biden Center](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Penn_Biden_Center).[\\[646\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-665)[\\[647\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-nytbatch1-666) According to the White House, the documents were reported to the [U.S. National Archives](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/U.S._National_Archives), which recovered them the next day.[\\[647\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-nytbatch1-666) On November 14, Attorney General [Merrick Garland](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Merrick_Garland) appointed [John R. Lausch Jr.](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_R._Lausch_Jr.) to conduct an investigation.[\\[648\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-667)[\\[649\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-668) On December 20, a second batch of classified documents was discovered in the garage of Biden\'s [Wilmington](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wilmington,_Delaware) residence.[\\[650\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-669)\n\nOn January 12, Garland appointed [Robert K. Hur](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Robert_K._Hur) as special counsel to investigate "possible unauthorized removal and retention of classified documents or other records".[\\[651\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-670) On January 20, after a 13-hour [consensual search](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Consent_search) by FBI investigators, six more items with classified markings were recovered from Biden\'s Wilmington residence.[\\[652\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-671) FBI agents searched Biden\'s home in [Rehoboth Beach](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rehoboth_Beach,_Delaware) on February 1 and collected papers from his time as vice president, but did not find any classified information.[\\[653\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-672) On February 8, 2024, Hur announced that no charges would be brought against Biden.[\\[654\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-673)\n\n#### Business activities\n\nMain article: [United States House Oversight Committee investigation into the Biden family](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_House_Oversight_Committee_investigation_into_the_Biden_family)\n\nFurther information: [Impeachment inquiry into Joe Biden](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Impeachment_inquiry_into_Joe_Biden)\n\nOn January 11, 2023, the [House of Representatives](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_House_of_Representatives) launched [an investigative committee](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_House_Oversight_Committee_investigation_into_the_Biden_family) into the foreign business activities of Biden\'s son, [Hunter](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hunter_Biden), and brother, [James](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/James_Biden).[\\[655\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-674) The committee\'s chair, Representative [James Comer](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/James_Comer), simultaneously investigated alleged corruption related to the [Hunter Biden laptop controversy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hunter_Biden_laptop_controversy).[\\[656\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-675)\n\nOn September 12, House speaker [Kevin McCarthy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kevin_McCarthy) initiated a formal impeachment inquiry against Biden, saying that the House investigations "paint a picture of corruption" by Biden and his family.[\\[t\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-680) Congressional investigations, including [by the House Oversight committee](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_House_Oversight_Committee_investigation_into_the_Biden_family), have discovered no evidence of wrongdoing by Biden as of December 2023.[\\[u\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-685) On December 13, 2023, the [House of Representatives](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_House_of_Representatives) voted 221–212 to formalize an [impeachment inquiry into Biden](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Impeachment_inquiry_into_Joe_Biden).[\\[665\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-686)[\\[666\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-687)[\\[667\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-688)\n\nIn February 2024, [Alexander Smirnov](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alexander_Smirnov_(FBI_informant)), a former intelligence [informant](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Informant) who was prominent in the bribery allegations against Biden, was charged with [making false statements](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Making_false_statements).[\\[668\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-689) Smirnov admitted he had publicized a false story given to him by Russian intelligence officials with the goal of damaging Biden\'s reelection campaign.[\\[669\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-690)[\\[670\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-691)[\\[671\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-692)\n\n### Age and health concerns\n\nMain article: [Age and health concerns about Joe Biden](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Age_and_health_concerns_about_Joe_Biden)\n\nBiden\'s 81st birthday cake\n\nAs of 2025, Biden was the oldest sitting president in U.S. history. His cognitive health was perceived to have declined by Republicans and some media figures,[\\[672\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-693)[\\[673\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-cbsjuly1age-694) and privately by some Democrats. Members of Biden\'s family and White House staffers insulated Biden from scrutiny of his advanced aging and decline in acuity.[\\[674\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-695)[\\[675\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-wsjagedec-696)[\\[676\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-697)\n\nThe media widely covered public concern about Biden\'s mental acuity after a weak performance in a June 2024 presidential debate,[\\[673\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-cbsjuly1age-694) but gave it limited coverage beforehand, in part due to harsh pushback from White House officials.[\\[677\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-698) Biden initially deemed himself fit to serve two terms as president,[\\[678\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-699) but after the 2024 election said that he may have been too old to serve a second term.[\\[679\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-700)\n\nAs part of the [investigation into Biden\'s handling of classified documents](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Joe_Biden_classified_documents_incident), special counsel [Robert Hur](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Robert_Hur) said that Biden did not remember when he was vice president ("if it was 2013—when did I stop being vice president?") or when his son Beau died.[\\[680\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-701) Hur wrote that his memory "appeared to have significant limitations".[\\[681\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-702)\n\nOn July 21, 2022, Biden tested positive for [COVID-19](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/COVID-19) with reportedly mild symptoms.[\\[682\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-703)[\\[683\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-AP_News-704) According to the White House, he was treated with [Paxlovid](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Paxlovid).[\\[683\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-AP_News-704)[\\[684\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-705) He worked in isolation in the White House for five days[\\[685\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-706) and returned to isolation when he tested positive again on July 30.[\\[686\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-707)[\\[687\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-708) On July 17, 2024, Biden again tested positive for COVID-19.[\\[688\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-709)[\\[689\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-710) In 2023, Biden was asked whether any other Democrats could beat Donald Trump. His response was "Probably 50 of them".[\\[690\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-711)\n\n## 2024 presidential campaign\n\nMain article: [Joe Biden 2024 presidential campaign](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Joe_Biden_2024_presidential_campaign)\n\nFurther information: [2024 Democratic Party presidential primaries](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2024_Democratic_Party_presidential_primaries), [Abandon Biden](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Abandon_Biden), [2024 Joe Biden–Donald Trump presidential debate](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2024_Joe_Biden%E2%80%93Donald_Trump_presidential_debate), and [Withdrawal of Joe Biden from the 2024 United States presidential election](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Withdrawal_of_Joe_Biden_from_the_2024_United_States_presidential_election)\n\nBiden addressing the nation after [his withdrawal](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Withdrawal_of_Joe_Biden_from_the_2024_United_States_presidential_election)\n\nEnding months of speculation,[\\[691\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-712)[\\[692\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-713) on April 25, 2023, Biden confirmed he would run for reelection as president in the [2024 election](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2024_United_States_presidential_election), with Harris again as his running mate.[\\[693\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-Associated_Press-714) On the day of his announcement, a Gallup poll found that Biden\'s approval rating was 37 percent, with most of those surveyed saying the economy was their biggest concern.[\\[694\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-pollrui-715) During his campaign, Biden promoted [higher economic growth and recovery](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Economic_policy_of_the_Joe_Biden_administration).[\\[695\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-716)[\\[696\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-717) He frequently stated his intention to "finish the job" as a political rallying cry.[\\[693\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-Associated_Press-714)[\\[697\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-718)[\\[698\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-719)\n\n[U.S. Representative](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/U.S._Representative) [Dean Phillips](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dean_Phillips) ran against Biden in the 2024 Democratic presidential primaries.[\\[699\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-720) Phillips [campaigned](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dean_Phillips_2024_presidential_campaign) as a younger alternative to Biden,[\\[700\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-721) who would be a stronger opponent to Trump in the general election.[\\[701\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-722)[\\[702\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-723) Biden was not on the ballot in the January 23, [New Hampshire primary](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2024_New_Hampshire_Democratic_presidential_primary), but won it in a write-in campaign with 63.8% of the vote.[\\[703\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-724) He had wanted South Carolina to be the first primary, and [won that state on February 3](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2024_South_Carolina_Democratic_presidential_primary) with 96.2% of the vote.[\\[704\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-725) Biden received 89.3% of the vote in [Nevada](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2024_Nevada_Democratic_presidential_primary) and 81.1% of the vote in [Michigan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2024_Michigan_Democratic_presidential_primary). On March 5 ("Super Tuesday"), he won 15 of 16 primaries, netting 80% or more of the vote in 13.[\\[705\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-726)[\\[706\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-727) Biden lost the [American Samoa](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2024_American_Samoa_Democratic_presidential_caucuses) contest to venture capitalist [Jason Palmer](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jason_Palmer_(politician)), becoming the first incumbent president to lose a contest while appearing on the ballot since [Jimmy Carter](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jimmy_Carter) in [1980](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1980_Democratic_Party_presidential_primaries).[\\[707\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-728) On March 6, Phillips suspended his campaign and endorsed Biden.[\\[708\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-729) On March 12, Biden reached more than the 1,968 delegates needed to win the Democratic nomination, becoming the presumptive nominee.[\\[709\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-730)[\\[710\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-731)[\\[711\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-732)\n\nThe [first presidential debate](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2024_Joe_Biden%E2%80%93Donald_Trump_presidential_debate) was held on June 27, 2024, between Biden and Trump. Biden\'s performance was widely criticized, with commentators saying he frequently lost his train of thought and gave meandering answers.[\\[712\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-reuters-biden-debate-733)[\\[713\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-apjune27-734)[\\[714\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-PoliticoJune28Dems-735) Several newspaper columnists declared Trump the winner,[\\[v\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-740) and polling indicated the majority of viewers believed Trump won.[\\[719\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-741) After the debate raised questions about [his health and age](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Age_and_health_concerns_of_Joe_Biden), Biden faced calls to withdraw from the race, including from [fellow Democrats](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_Democrats_who_opposed_the_Joe_Biden_2024_presidential_campaign)[\\[720\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-nbc-biden-step-down-742) and the [editorial boards](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Editorial_boards) of several major news outlets.[\\[721\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-:0-743)[\\[722\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-744)\n\nBiden and President-elect Donald Trump meet in the [Oval Office](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Oval_Office) as part of the [presidential transition](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Second_presidential_transition_of_Donald_Trump) on November 13, 2024.\n\nBiden initially insisted that he would remain a candidate,[\\[723\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-745) but on July 21, he withdrew his candidacy, writing that this was "in the best interest of my party and the country".[\\[724\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-746) He endorsed Harris as his successor.[\\[725\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-747)[\\[726\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-748) On August 6, 2024, Harris was confirmed as the Democratic presidential nominee.[\\[727\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-749) This was the first time an eligible incumbent had declined to run for reelection since [1968](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1968_United_States_presidential_election).[\\[728\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-750)\n\nIn the general election, Trump defeated Harris. The Senate [went Republican](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2024_United_States_Senate_elections) for the first time since 2018. In a nationally televised speech after the election, Biden congratulated Trump and promised a "peaceful and orderly" transition of power.[\\[729\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-751) In a January 2025 interview, Biden claimed he could have defeated Trump had he not been persuaded to withdraw from the election, despite lagging behind Trump in polling.[\\[730\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-752)[\\[731\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-753) A [YouGov](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/YouGov) poll conducted on November 6–7, 2024, found that if Biden had been the Democratic nominee, Trump would have won the popular vote by 49% to 42%. Trump won the popular vote over Harris by 49.8% to 48.3%.[\\[732\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-754)\n\n## Post-presidency (2025–present)\n\nBiden attending the funeral of Dick Cheney in November 2025\n\nBiden\'s term ended on January 20, 2025.[\\[733\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-755) At the end of his presidency, Biden designated former [senior advisors](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Senior_Advisor_to_the_President_of_the_United_States) [Anthony Bernal](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Anthony_Bernal) and [Annie Tomasini](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Annie_Tomasini) to raise funds for the [Joseph R. Biden Jr. Presidential Library](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Joseph_R._Biden_Jr._Presidential_Library).[\\[734\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-756) He later signed with talent agency [Creative Artists Agency](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Creative_Artists_Agency) (CAA), which previously represented him from 2017 to 2020.[\\[735\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-757)[\\[736\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-758)\n\nOn February 7, President Trump revoked Biden\'s security clearance.[\\[737\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-759) Former presidents have traditionally been granted access to intelligence briefings, though such access is at the sitting president\'s discretion. In 2021, Biden had revoked Trump\'s security clearance for his role in inciting the [January 6 Capitol attack](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/January_6_Capitol_attack).[\\[738\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-760)[\\[739\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-761)\n\nOn April 15, Biden made his first major public appearance since leaving office, delivering remarks at an Advocates, Counselors and Representatives for the Disabled (ACRD) conference in [Chicago](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chicago).[\\[740\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-762) In his address, he criticized the Trump administration\'s handling of the Social Security Administration.[\\[741\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-763) On May 7, Biden appeared on _[The View](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_View)_ to defend his presidential legacy.[\\[742\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-764)\n\nOn April 26, Biden and his wife attended the state funeral of [Pope Francis](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pope_Francis) in Vatican City.[\\[743\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-765)\n\nOn September 6, Biden announced that his proposed [presidential center](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Joseph_R._Biden_Jr._Presidential_Library) would be in Delaware and that he and his foundation had approved a 13-person governance board.[\\[744\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-766)\n\nOn his 83rd birthday, November 20, 2025, Biden and his wife attended former U.S. vice president [Dick Cheney](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dick_Cheney)\'s funeral.[\\[745\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-767)\n\n### Health\n\nOn May 18, 2025, Biden\'s office announced that he had been diagnosed with aggressive [prostate cancer](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Prostate_cancer) with [bone metastasis](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bone_metastasis) during a routine physical examination.[\\[746\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-768) On May 30, Biden confirmed that he had begun treatment.[\\[747\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-769)\n\nBiden’s office stated that his last known [prostate-specific antigen](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Prostate-specific_antigen) (PSA) screening had occurred in 2014, more than a decade before his diagnosis.[\\[748\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-770)[\\[749\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-771) Following the announcement, several medical experts noted that prostate cancers of this type can progress undetected for many years.[\\[750\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-:3-772)[\\[751\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-773) Some [oncologists](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Oncologists) argued that Biden had likely developed the disease well before 2025, with one expert stating that he “did not develop it in the last 100 or 200 days” and had probably had cancer during the early years of his presidency.[\\[752\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-774) Other medical analysts emphasized that changes in PSA-screening guidelines for men over 70 made long gaps in testing common, complicating efforts to determine when the cancer first emerged.[\\[750\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-:3-772)\n\nOn September 4, Biden\'s spokesperson confirmed that he had recently undergone [Mohs surgery](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mohs_surgery) to remove skin cancer lesions from his forehead. The procedure followed a 2023 removal of a [basal-cell carcinoma](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Basal-cell_carcinoma) from his chest.[\\[753\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-775)\n\nOn October 11, Biden\'s spokesperson confirmed that he was undergoing [radiation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Radiation_therapy) and [hormone therapies](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hormonal_therapy_(oncology)) for his prostate cancer.[\\[754\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-776) On October 20, Biden completed a course of radiation therapy at Penn Medicine Radiation Oncology at the [University of Pennsylvania](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/University_of_Pennsylvania); it is uncertain whether he will need further treatment.[\\[755\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-bidenhealth-777)[\\[756\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-778)\n\n## Political positions\n\nMain portal](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Portal:United_States) |\n\n[Pope Francis](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pope_Francis) (left) meets Joe Biden at the White House, September 2015.\n\nAs a senator, Biden was regarded as a [moderate Democrat](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moderate_Democrat).[\\[757\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-779) As a presidential nominee, Biden\'s platform had been called the most progressive of any major party platform in history, although not within his party\'s ideological vanguard.[\\[758\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-780) Biden says his positions are deeply influenced by [Catholic social teaching](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Catholic_social_teaching).[\\[759\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-781)[\\[760\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-782)[\\[761\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-783)\n\nAccording to political scientist Carlo Invernizzi Accetti, Biden represents an Americanized form of [Christian democracy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Christian_democracy), taking positions characteristic of both the [center-right](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Center-right) and [center-left](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Center-left).[\\[762\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-Foreign_Policy-784) Biden has cited the Catholic philosopher [Jacques Maritain](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jacques_Maritain), credited with starting the Christian democratic movement, as immensely influential in his thinking.[\\[763\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-785) Other analysts have likened his ideology to traditional [liberalism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Modern_liberalism_in_the_United_States), "a doctrine of liberty, equality, justice and individual rights that relies... on a strong federal government for enforcement".[\\[764\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-Greenberg-786) In 2022, journalist [Sasha Issenberg](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sasha_Issenberg) wrote that Biden\'s "most valuable political skill" was "an innate compass for the ever-shifting mainstream of the Democratic Party".[\\[765\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-787) Some critics claimed Biden\'s climate policy was [socialist](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Socialism).[\\[766\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-788)[\\[767\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-789)[\\[768\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-790)\n\nBiden proposed partially reversing the corporate tax cuts of the [Tax Cuts and Jobs Act of 2017](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tax_Cuts_and_Jobs_Act_of_2017).[\\[769\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-791)[\\[770\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-792) He voted for the [North American Free Trade Agreement](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/North_American_Free_Trade_Agreement) (NAFTA)[\\[771\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-793) and the [Trans-Pacific Partnership](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Trans-Pacific_Partnership).[\\[772\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-794) Biden is a staunch supporter of the [Affordable Care Act](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Affordable_Care_Act) (ACA).[\\[773\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-ACA203-795)[\\[774\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-796) He promoted a plan to build upon it,[\\[773\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-ACA203-795) aiming to expand [health insurance coverage](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Health_insurance_coverage_in_the_United_States) to 97% of Americans, including by creating a [public health insurance option](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Public_health_insurance_option).[\\[775\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-797)\n\nBiden did not support national [same-sex marriage](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Same-sex_marriage) rights while in the Senate and voted for the [Defense of Marriage Act](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Defense_of_Marriage_Act),[\\[776\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-798) but opposed proposals for constitutional amendments that would have banned same-sex marriage nationwide.[\\[777\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-799) Biden has supported same-sex marriage since 2012.[\\[95\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-NYT_Biden_Evolution_on_LGBTQ-98)[\\[778\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-800) As a senator, Biden forged deep relationships with police groups and was a chief proponent of a [Police Officer\'s Bill of Rights](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Law_Enforcement_Officers%27_Bill_of_Rights) measure that police unions supported but police chiefs opposed.[\\[779\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-801)[\\[780\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-802) In 2020, Biden also ran on decriminalizing [cannabis](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cannabis),[\\[781\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-803) after advocating harsher penalties for drug use as a senator.[\\[782\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-804)[\\[783\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-805)\n\nBiden believes action must be taken on [climate change](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change). As a senator, he co-sponsored the [Boxer–Sanders Global Warming Pollution Reduction Act](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Global_Warming_Pollution_Reduction_Act_of_2007), the most stringent climate bill in the [United States Senate](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_Senate).[\\[784\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-806) Biden supports [nature conservation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nature_conservation). According to a report from the [Center for American Progress](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Center_for_American_Progress), he broke several records in this domain.[\\[785\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-807) He took steps to protect [old-growth forests](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Old-growth_forest).[\\[786\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-808) Biden opposes drilling for oil in the [Arctic National Wildlife Refuge](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arctic_National_Wildlife_Refuge).[\\[787\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-809) He wants to achieve a carbon-free power sector in the U.S. by 2035 and stop emissions completely by 2050.[\\[788\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-810) His program included reentering the [Paris Agreement](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Paris_Agreement), [green building](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Green_building) and more.[\\[789\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-811) Biden supports [environmental justice](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Environmental_justice), including [climate justice](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_justice) and [ocean justice](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Blue_justice).[\\[w\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-816) Biden called global temperature rise above the 1.5°C limit the "only existential threat humanity faces even more frightening than a nuclear war".[\\[794\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-817) Despite his clean energy policies and congressional Republicans characterizing them as a "War on American Energy", domestic oil production reached a record high in October 2023.[\\[795\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-818)\n\nBiden has said the U.S. needs to "get tough" on China, calling it the "most serious competitor" that poses challenges to the United States\' "prosperity, security, and democratic values".[\\[796\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-819)[\\[797\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-820) Biden has spoken about human rights abuses in the [Xinjiang](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Xinjiang) region to Chinese leader [Xi Jinping](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Xi_Jinping), pledging to sanction and commercially restrict Chinese government officials and entities who carry out repression.[\\[798\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-821)[\\[799\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-822) Biden has said he is against [regime change](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Regime_change) but is for providing non-military support to opposition movements.[\\[800\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-823) He opposed direct U.S. [intervention in Libya](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2011_military_intervention_in_Libya),[\\[801\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-824)[\\[205\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-The_New_York_Times-2-209) voted against U.S. participation in the [Gulf War](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gulf_War),[\\[802\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-825) voted in favor of the [Iraq War](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iraq_War),[\\[803\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-826) and supports a [two-state solution](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Two-state_solution) in the [Israeli–Palestinian conflict](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israeli%E2%80%93Palestinian_conflict).[\\[804\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-827) Biden pledged to end U.S. support for the [Saudi Arabian-led intervention in Yemen](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Saudi_Arabian-led_intervention_in_Yemen) and to reevaluate the [United States\' relationship](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Saudi_Arabia%E2%80%93United_States_relations) with [Saudi Arabia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Saudi_Arabia).[\\[261\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-foreign-policy2-266) Biden supported extending the [New START](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/New_START) arms control treaty with Russia to limit the number of [nuclear weapons](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nuclear_weapon) deployed by both sides.[\\[805\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-828)[\\[806\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-829) In 2021, Biden officially [recognized](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Armenian_genocide_recognition) the [Armenian genocide](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Armenian_genocide), becoming the first U.S. president to do so.[\\[807\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-830)[\\[x\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-833)\n\nBiden supported [abortion rights](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Abortion-rights_movements) throughout his presidency, though he personally opposes abortion because of his Catholic faith.[\\[810\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-834)[\\[811\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-835) In 2019, he said he supported _[Roe v. Wade](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Roe_v._Wade)_ and repealing the [Hyde Amendment](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hyde_Amendment).[\\[812\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-836)[\\[813\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-837) After _[Dobbs v. Jackson Women\'s Health Organization](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dobbs_v._Jackson_Women%27s_Health_Organization)_, he criticized [near-total bans on abortion access](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Abortion_law_in_the_United_States_by_state) passed in a majority of [Republican](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Republican_Party_(United_States))-controlled states,[\\[814\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-838) and took measures to protect [abortion rights in the United States](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Abortion_in_the_United_States).[\\[815\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-839) Biden rejected calls to provide abortion services on [federal land](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Federal_lands).[\\[816\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-840)[\\[817\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-841) He vowed to sign a bill codifying the protections of _Roe_ into federal law; such a bill passed the House in 2022, but was unable to clear the Senate filibuster.[\\[818\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-842)[\\[819\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-843)\n\n## Public image\n\nMain article: [Public image of Joe Biden](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Public_image_of_Joe_Biden)\n\nBiden was consistently ranked one of the least wealthy [members of the Senate](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_Senate),[\\[820\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-844)[\\[821\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-845) which he attributed to having been elected young.[\\[822\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-846) Feeling that less-wealthy public officials may be tempted to accept contributions in exchange for political favors, he proposed [campaign finance reform](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Campaign_finance_reform_in_the_United_States) measures during his first term.[\\[85\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-cby-44-88) While a senator, Biden was viewed as being close to the credit card company [MBNA](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/MBNA), a major contributor to his campaigns since 1989, sometimes being called the "senator from MBNA".[\\[823\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-847) As of November\xa02009[\\[update\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Joe_Biden&action=edit), Biden\'s net worth was $27,012.[\\[824\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-848) By November 2020[\\[update\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Joe_Biden&action=edit), the Bidens were worth $9 million, largely due to sales of Biden\'s books and speaking fees after his vice presidency.[\\[825\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-849)[\\[826\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-850)\n\nPolitical columnist [David S. Broder](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/David_S._Broder) wrote that Biden has grown over time: "He responds to real people—that\'s been consistent throughout. And his ability to understand himself and deal with other politicians has gotten much, much better."[\\[33\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-watn020109-35) Journalist [James Traub](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/James_Traub) has written that "Biden is the kind of fundamentally happy person who can be as generous toward others as he is to himself".[\\[126\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-nytm-traub-129) Particularly since the 2015 death of his elder son Beau, Biden has been noted for his empathetic nature and ability to communicate about grief.[\\[827\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-851)[\\[828\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-852)\n\nJournalist and TV anchor [Wolf Blitzer](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wolf_Blitzer) has called Biden loquacious;[\\[829\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-853) journalist Mark Bowden has said that he is famous for "talking too much", leaning in close "like an old pal with something urgent to tell you".[\\[288\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-The_Atlantic-293) He often deviates from prepared remarks,[\\[830\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-854) and sometimes "puts his foot in his mouth".[\\[162\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-nyt-no2-166)[\\[831\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-855)[\\[832\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-856) Biden has a reputation for being prone to [gaffes](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Political_gaffe).[\\[833\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-857)[\\[834\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-858)[\\[835\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-859) _The New York Times_ wrote that Biden\'s "weak filters make him capable of blurting out pretty much anything".[\\[162\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-nyt-no2-166)\n\nAccording to _The New York Times_, Biden often embellishes elements of his life or exaggerates, a trait also noted by _[The New Yorker](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_New_Yorker)_ in 2014.[\\[836\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-The_New_Yorker-860)[\\[837\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-The_New_York_Times-861) For instance, he has claimed to have been more active in the [civil rights movement](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Civil_rights_movement) than he actually was, and has falsely recalled being an excellent student who earned three college degrees.[\\[836\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-The_New_Yorker-860) The _Times_ wrote, "Mr. Biden\'s folksiness can veer into folklore, with dates that don\'t quite add up and details that are exaggerated or wrong, the factual edges shaved off to make them more powerful for audiences."[\\[837\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-The_New_York_Times-861)\n\n### Job approval\n\nSee also: [2021](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2021_opinion_polling_on_the_Biden_administration), [2022](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_opinion_polling_on_the_Biden_administration), [2023](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2023_opinion_polling_on_the_Biden_administration), and [2024–2025 opinion polling on the Biden administration](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2024%E2%80%932025_opinion_polling_on_the_Biden_administration)\n\nAccording to [Morning Consult](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Morning_Consult) polling, Biden maintained an [approval rating](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Opinion_poll) above 50% during his presidency\'s first eight months. In August 2021, it began to decline, reaching the low forties by December.[\\[838\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-862) This was attributed to the Afghanistan withdrawal, increasing hospitalizations from the [Delta variant](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/SARS-CoV-2_Delta_variant), [high inflation and gas prices](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2021%E2%80%932023_inflation_surge), disarray within the Democratic Party, and a general decline in popularity customary in politics.[\\[y\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-867) In 2023, Biden\'s approval rating was the lowest of any modern[\\[z\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-868) U.S. president after three years in office.[\\[843\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-gallup2023end-869)\n\n[Gallup, Inc.](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gallup,_Inc.) found Biden\'s approval ratings to be consistently above 50% during his first few months in office,[\\[844\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-Gallup_Approval-870)[\\[845\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-871) but by August, his ratings began to decline.[\\[846\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-872) He had a 98% approval rating from Democrats in February 2021, but by December only 78% approved of his presidency.[\\[847\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-BidenGallup-873)[\\[844\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-Gallup_Approval-870) By October 2023, his rating among Democrats had reached a record low of 75%.[\\[843\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-gallup2023end-869)[\\[848\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-874) His approval rating among Republicans has been consistently in the single digits, aside from his first few months in office.[\\[847\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-BidenGallup-873) Additionally, Gallup noted that Biden\'s public support eroded each year he was in office: he averaged 49% approval in his first year,[\\[849\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-875) 41% in his second,[\\[850\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-876) 40% in his third,[\\[851\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-877) and 39% in his fourth.[\\[852\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-gallup20250117-878) In July 2024, just before he withdrew from the 2024 presidential election, Gallup found his approval rating had fallen to an all-time low of 36%.[\\[853\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-879) Gallup found that Biden had an average approval rating of 42.2% throughout his presidency, which was lower than all other presidents\' except Trump\'s first term, at 41.1%. Biden\'s final approval rating in January 2025 was 40%, which was low but still higher than several other presidents\' final approval ratings.[\\[852\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-gallup20250117-878) Gallup\'s averaged polls of Biden\'s presidency found that he was the second-least popular president in its polling history, ahead of Trump.[\\[852\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-gallup20250117-878)\n\nCNN and CBS News found Biden\'s final approval rating to be 37% and 36%, respectively.[\\[854\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-880)[\\[855\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-881) Polling aggregator [FiveThirtyEight](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/FiveThirtyEight) found that Biden had a final average approval rating of 37%.[\\[856\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-882)\n\n### Media depictions\n\nSee also: [_Saturday Night Live_ parodies of Joe Biden](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Saturday_Night_Live_parodies_of_Joe_Biden)\n\nNine men have portrayed Biden on _[Saturday Night Live](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Saturday_Night_Live)_, starting with [Kevin Nealon](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kevin_Nealon) in 1991. [Jason Sudeikis](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jason_Sudeikis) portrayed Biden during the 2008 election season and reprised the role many times. During the 2020 election season, Biden was played by [John Mulaney](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_Mulaney), [Alex Moffat](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alex_Moffat), [Mikey Day](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mikey_Day), [Woody Harrelson](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Woody_Harrelson), and [Jim Carrey](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jim_Carrey). In 2024, [Dana Carvey](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dana_Carvey) played the role.[\\[857\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-883)[\\[858\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-884) In 2016, [Greg Kinnear](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Greg_Kinnear) portrayed Biden in the [HBO](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/HBO) television film _[Confirmation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Confirmation_(film))_, about the [Clarence Thomas Supreme Court nomination hearings](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Clarence_Thomas_Supreme_Court_nomination).[\\[859\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-885)\n\nBiden appears in episodes of _[Parks and Recreation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Parks_and_Recreation)_ during his time as vice president.[\\[860\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-886) He appears as himself in a 2016 episode of _[Law & Order: SVU](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Law_%26_Order:_Special_Victims_Unit)_.[\\[861\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-887)\n\n_[The Onion](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Onion)_ featured a series of articles about a [fictionalized Joe Biden](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Joe_Biden_(The_Onion)).[\\[862\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-888)[\\[863\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-889)\n\n## Assessments\n\nA December 2024 Gallup poll found that 54% of Americans thought Biden\'s presidency was below average or poor, 26% average, and 19% above average or outstanding.[\\[864\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-890) Gallup found that Americans largely offered negative assessments of Biden\'s presidency on economic, national, and international issues. Of 18 issue areas Gallup tracked, a majority of Americans said the U.S. lost ground in six, including the economy in general, immigration, and the country\'s position in the world. A plurality found that the U.S. declined in six other areas, including national infrastructure and energy, education, and trade relations with other countries. A plurality felt the U.S. made progress in only one indicator under Biden: the conditions of [gay, lesbian, and transgender people](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/LGBTQ_people).[\\[865\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-891)\n\nJournalist [Amy Walter](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Amy_Walter), editor of the nonpartisan _[The Cook Political Report](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Cook_Political_Report)_, argued that the public deemed Biden\'s presidency a failure particularly due to frustration over inflation. Walter said that voters considered inflation the most important element of the economy, more important than the stock market, low unemployment, or household income.[\\[866\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-892) Economists debate the extent to which Biden\'s policies were responsible for inflation,[\\[867\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-893) but according to Gallup, public perception of the economy in 2024 was worse only in 2008 and 1992, helping Trump win the 2024 presidential election.[\\[868\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-894)\n\nThe [Siena College Research Institute](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Siena_College_Research_Institute)\'s 2022 survey [ranked Biden](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Historical_rankings_of_presidents_of_the_United_States#2022_Siena_College) 19th out of 45 presidents.[\\[869\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-895) The 2024 _Presidential Greatness Project Expert_ survey ranked Biden the 14th-best president.[\\[870\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-bc-896) A February 2024 [American Political Science Association](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/American_Political_Science_Association) poll of historians and scholars ranked Biden the 14th-greatest president, diverging from public assessments. The pollsters noted that Biden\'s ranking was unusually high for a presidency without military victories or institutional expansion. The experts polled generally regarded Biden\'s signature accomplishment as his victory over Trump in the 2020 election, which was perceived as helping to protect and restore political and institutional norms in U.S. government.[\\[871\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-897)[\\[872\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-898)[\\[870\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-bc-896)\n\nWhen Biden left office in 2025, journalists and many Democrats viewed his presidency as a failure due to [age and health concerns](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Age_and_health_concerns_about_Joe_Biden), public frustration over inflation, and Harris\'s loss to Trump in the [2024 presidential election](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2024_United_States_presidential_election).[\\[873\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-899) _[The Guardian](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Guardian)_ called the conclusion of Biden\'s presidency a "tragedy", particularly because Biden was succeeded by Trump after previously defeating him.[\\[874\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-900) Journalist [Ronald Brownstein](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ronald_Brownstein) compared Biden to [Jimmy Carter](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jimmy_Carter): Biden\'s presidency was overshadowed by the [2021–2023 inflation surge](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2021%E2%80%932023_inflation_surge), much as the [1970s energy crisis](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1970s_energy_crisis) and [stagflation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Stagflation) overshadowed [Carter\'s presidency](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Presidency_of_Jimmy_Carter). Both men were Democrats and served a single term as president.[\\[875\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-901) [Biden\'s withdrawal from the 2024 presidential election](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Withdrawal_of_Joe_Biden_from_the_2024_United_States_presidential_election) was compared to [Lyndon B. Johnson\'s withdrawal from the 1968 presidential election](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Withdrawal_of_Lyndon_B._Johnson_from_the_1968_United_States_presidential_election).[\\[876\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-902)[\\[877\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-903)[\\[878\\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_note-904)\n\n## **[^](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org#cite_ref-539)**[Kyrsten Sinema](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kyrsten_Sinema) and [Joe Manchin](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Joe_Manchin), whose seats As a result, 47Democrats (rather than 49), plus [Angus King](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Angus_King) and [Bernie Sanders](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bernie_Sanders), independents who caucus with Democrats, were in the Senate of the [118th United States Congress](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/118th_United_States_Congress), on May31, 2024. Manchin continued to caucus with Democrats while Sinema opted to caucus with neither party but to align with the Democrats, bringing the Democratic Senate majority to containing video clips](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Category:Articles_containing_video_clips)\n\nSearch\n\nSearch\n\nJoe Biden\n\n225 languages [Add topic](https://en.wikipedia.org/en.wikipedia.org)', title='Joe Biden - Wikipedia', url='https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Joe_Biden'), WebSearchResult(content="Main Content\n\nJoseph Robinette Biden, Jr. was born on November 20, 1942, in Scranton, Pennsylvania. In 1953, the Biden family moved to Delaware. Biden later graduated from the University of Delaware and Syracuse Law School. In 1972, at the age of 29, he was elected to the United States Senate.1\n\nSeveral weeks after the election, Biden's wife Neilia and daughter Naomi died in a tragic car accident; their two young sons, Joseph “Beau” III and Hunter, were also seriously injured. Biden took the Oath of Office at the hospital and began commuting to Washington by train, a practice he maintained throughout his Senate career. In 1977, Biden married Jill Jacobs, and the couple raised Beau and Hunter. In 1980, they welcomed a daughter, Ashley.2\n\nAs chairman and ranking member of the Senate Judiciary Committee, Biden was recognized for his work on criminal justice, including the 1994 Crime Act and the Violence Against Women Act. As chairman or ranking member of the Senate Foreign Relations Committee, Biden played a pivotal role in shaping U.S. foreign policy. He served thirty-six years in the United States Senate.3\n\nIn 2008, presidential candidate Barack Obama chose Biden as his running mate, and they won the election that November. Vice President Biden implemented the American Recovery and Reinvestment Act, led several initiatives to reduce violence against women, and initiated the “Cancer Moonshot” program after Beau’s death from brain cancer.4 On January 12, 2017, President Obama awarded Vice President Biden the Presidential Medal of Freedom for his decades of public service.5\n\nIn 2020, Biden returned to politics to challenge and defeat President Donald J. Trump. Biden was the first president from Delaware and the second Roman Catholic president in United States history. During the campaign, Biden selected Kamala Harris as his running mate. Harris was the first woman, first African American, and first person of South Asian heritage to serve as Vice President of the United States.6\n\nPresident Biden’s immediate priorities included expanding relief programs and ensuring public safety with the COVID-19 pandemic, boosting the American economy, and strengthening traditional alliances. The administration worked with Congress to pass several major pieces of legislation that provided funding to improve infrastructure and high-speed internet access; invest in clean energy production; expand access to health insurance; and lower prescription drug and insulin costs.7 President Biden also made history when he nominated Kentanji Brown Jackson – the first Black woman to serve on the United States Supreme Court.\n\nOn the world stage, President Biden condemned Russian aggression and supported Ukrainian resistance. He ordered the withdrawal of U.S. troops from Afghanistan, ending America’s longest war but the operation and subsequent fallout were heavily criticized. In July 2024, President Biden withdrew from the presidential race and supported Vice President Harris as the nominee.\n\nSee Footnotes & Resources\n\n## Footnotes & Resources\n\n1.
